Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which some manner thus is that thou makest III cauteries, or IIII, in aligning according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not hasten thy hand to the whole cautery, and let the patient be lying on his back; and another manner of cautery thus is that thou heatest the cautery which has II ners, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is opposite the mouse, or the cuts of the patient come from the left, and let the elevation which thou liftest the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he sets the two nerves inflamed until the kernels are pierced on the other side, and then withdraws the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see, then cauterize the entire cautery to three nerves.  
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before said. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy 
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for edema, except for the method called “asclytes.” 
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make IIII cautery around the belly, and I on the stomach, and one on the liver, and I on the spleen, and II behind the back on the spine, and I place the hip; and let the cauteries be close to the heart.  
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery uncovered for to fight rot long time, and do not leave the care of the ill after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the clavicle that we have in front; and for the back it is olive-shaped, according to what has been put here before. 
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in the one who is hydrophic and are full of a yellow-green fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep with it, thus close the opening around the white, and be the cautery according to this form. 
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make on II legs II cautery in each leg at the point of the cutellar; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open lengthwise without cure, that they may be in it; after the cure of the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	of the hand 
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of great virtue, then I make a great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, to the circular cautery; and four cauteries around the bud subtle to all the cautery clavicle subtle, and two cauteries on the haunches. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make cautery on the groin, and I cautery on each flank, and II small cauteries on the stomach near the great one, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.  
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids 
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or one or more, and they are old and are large cold and moist humors corrupted, and they are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you do cauteries: III on top of the spine of the back, that which is all outside of the armpit poke and poke in triangulating, and I cautery below the navel II; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees inflating the face, then to the face one makes a large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the spleen to the entire cautery clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the cartilage which is called "thelul" 
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the vein, immediately heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it fully ablaze on that vein; and let it remain as long as the cautery comes to the base of the vein, so that the blood does not run; do this once or twice, and if there is much blood, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cures of ointments beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the area, it will have more help. 
de plaie mal curee	of wound poorly cared for 
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such a disease that can be healed only by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and is filled and cast putridity and corrupted moisture, so the should prove at once a fine tent, and guard that you know at once the tent how much it has of width. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After having heated the cautery which seems like a razor, and having put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the thing entered there, and reheat the cautery until those corrupted bodies are burned, once or II or III times, according to the quantity of need; and be careful not to burn the nerves which are within, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, so keep away from these places, and make these fuers only in fleshy place, and think that it is not wholly diseased; after cure the place as long as it is healthy, and if the place is sailiez, and the matters are removed for a long time, then know that the place is healed entirely; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is rotten, and corrupted the bone at the root; and thus like one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes with heavy windiness and does not take much of woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the loins on one side and the other, with the cautery clavile that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more help. 
de la vessie	of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the span of a hand; and do the cauteries on the back, if it is necessary; and let the cauteries be pointed according to the form mentioned before. 
de la marris	of the wound 
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one makes three cauteries around the bud, as we have said of the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be strong, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip 
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place is found in the region below the waist, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like that with which the stomach has been cauterized. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make three cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip 
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the cure is not working, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say altogether hot medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cauterization of fire is done in many ways, some are such that you cauterize on the side of the hip III cauteries triangular according to this form, and make a good depth and large, and between each cautery space the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes cauteries in the middle on the top of the hip, so there are IIII according to this form:  
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart are burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg.  
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make II cautery there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and the cautery above the ankle IV two finger-breadths, on the left side a point; and be the cautery cuticular or be it burnt with the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers' breadth of the foot or near it, cauterize there where he feels the pain III points or IV at the cautery called "poins". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, if he does more; and if it is known that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, do cautery with a pointed or circular cautery, and be well careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much cautery that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not make more nuisance and contraction to the patient. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left them so that the leg was entirely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of belly from which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner. 
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said in the cautery of the hip, for this is the manner, make such iron and be at the chief also as big as a thimble, or a little less, and be by interweavings and be from one interweaving to the other of space the quantity of a fist knuckle; and be the interweavings toward two parts, and be also like nuts, and there is the hip of iron well made; and this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be cauterized until it is all red and swollen, and then place it on the side of the sick hip, and turn it toward the healthy side; and cauterize once the cautery reopens and let it for III days; and then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound covered long; after the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery for fear of its regard, and if we see few who use it; and nonetheless those are good cauteries, which can suffer it, and where it is affected. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine burning is that you make the instrument in pieces in which descends the edge of the door, and be of iron or steel to a length, and in the height has it two, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a coin; and be open below and above, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put on the boil of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand very on the boil of the hip; after throw between the II circles of the hot awl which be heated at the fire I poc, and let him one hour dou tens, and suffer the patient the heat and the burn of it. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is found also a cautery like fire; and when the cautery is passed, raise your hand with the instrument and lift the buttock gently, and leave it so for III days, and put butter on it until what is black from the scald is gone; and let it be for III days that rot may arise; and this would be the last help after the care of dressings until he is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, then you make the instrument that holds it as according to what you did in the hip augmentation; and this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it or treated of the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole burned so that the point of a knife can enter; and put one in the other well sealed, and put on top alkali and chalk and sweet oil on top, until it has a certain amount above the powders as you have grasped it well with your hand; and let it be like this until it descends sweet oil and cheese or well sealed, then take all that oil and throw it on top of chalk and alkali like before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very hot and is administered in works of medicine and cauteries of other members because it does work like fire, and if there are other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip well like honey, cassia, and wax with soap, all these things mixed together.  
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Gaius tells us about a cure of which one man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatica vein, and he spoke well, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed as he teaches afterwards. 
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in such manner that you take litargyre green fresh and dry, and grind it very well with a little bit of fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain holds, and the lesion; and let it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient feels no more burning.  
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until the body is a little bit aroused, and put him in his bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauteries of such medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with iron of goat, it helps a lot; and it must be done the cautery in such a manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and wet it with old oil, and put it on the socket which is between the thumb and the foot, and the other called fossa. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking fibers of dry goat, and set it on fire until it is charcoal, and put it on the wool, and let it be there until it cools; and do again like this, and do not cease to do like this until you think by sense that it comes up to the hip, and that the pain is stopped; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back 
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by too much evacuation, or by similar matter spread cold, none of these appearances is worth cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter. 
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after what the patient is void of fetid pills or other similar things, that on him be made upon his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see, make III cauteries or IIII at the clavical cautery middle according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to little children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a narrow back when they stand, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes above the other spines.  
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see these and you want to treat them, cauterize it with the cautery of this one according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine equally. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, so cauterize around the spine with a cautery that stings two or three lines, and let the points be near each other.  
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the wound as long as it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not administer cautery in a place that is in the space of nerves. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints are from humors that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is of cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you take hold upon the face of the foot, then do cauterize to the whole cautery as one claims "point."  
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you make a cautery on each knee III cauteries or IV of each part, to all the olive cautery; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand too hard except as long as the point of the heart is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the bone two lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and pondered medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh  
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin and the testicles descend to the thighs, and it is new, if you see them cure it, that they do not move that day. And let him use things that hold the belly up, so that the intestines descend from his belly; after he make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his arm outstretched as long as the testicles are repaired, and put them in your hands, and sign a cut below the rupture on the bone of the little finger, and all one sign that is like half a circle above the body; then ignite the cautery with this form: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it feels soft. 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return back; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other on the leg which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and the straight one and the one as far as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, redo it again until you come to the bone; and be careful that the bone does not jump out when you do the cautery; that you do not burn it; and so that the patient does not die, or another ailment. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of great people as large according to their measure; after III days cure their place of cautery with butter until the scalding is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie XL days on his back until the wound is well soldered; and it is necessary that his dressings be left long, so that the boil does not come out when he wants to go into chambers.  
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, administer to him a good splint, and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he does not work much and beware of too great repletion of drinking and eating, and of too much braising; and when he does this teaching, he is completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of tailoring in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come into other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, to them one makes the cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and either burn it at one-third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize with the cautery of three angles according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the place of the joint and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand amidst all the cautery clavicle 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is of no avail, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called «poins», and let the cauterization be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and of its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on that one, because it is customary that it must heal in the member that it is near to, so it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	of mashery 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are aided at times by cautery with great help, and even the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.  
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see him cauterized, take care that the patient is at the beginning, and if he is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not send nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole sick person, then make V cauteries on his head: I remove the chief to nine, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and II on the II horns, and I behind on the haiterel; and let your hand be so that the cauteries come until the bone, and as long as the scorches come out so that the vapors of the gross humors may issue from them; and cauterize it on the mice according to what it is before. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the miasma is spread everywhere; and it appears manifestly, then it befits that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and I cautery in its head, and II cautery on the spine of the neck, and VI cauteries on the spine of the back, and I on the knee and I other behind, and II on the two shoulders; and II on the elbows, and II on the tendons of the arm, and I on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard yourself from the nerves that are on the last calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cautery on the bone of the thigh, and I other on the bone of the stomach, and I other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when more cautery is done, the more it helps and benefits him; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as healthy people feel it, because the body is already wholly corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After care the place with flour of eggs with honey and other cures until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be a point going into the thickness of the skin; then cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at times one makes cautery with the hand and the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus it is removed the swelling; and all ways let no one interfere unless he is knowledgeable of the members and of the exits of the nerves moving the body. 
de albaras	of  bars 
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sickness called «albaras» is present and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery in one place, according to the quantity of the sharpness of the heart, until the blemish is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colocynth and blood of alondre, each one part; and let them all be mixed together, and be bound with a cloth, and be aired in place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of the sore by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with the cautery which seems like a circle, all around the border of the sore. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the wise men said that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the ulcer; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; and more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called 'circulus', as we have said in many cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be moved 
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati," and it takes time to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the blood of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it so. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through the whole cautery, so heat the cautery of this which is the form: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of the sickness which is called “adubelati” until the cautery has pierced the heart, and be such the cautery that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rot be lessened. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed.  
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron 
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is called "corroding," and it is nothing else than a corruption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs like fire consumes dry vines. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place where it can suffer cautery together with fire, then sharpen the cauteries small and large, according to what is necessary for the place where the illness is; after that cauterize from all sides as much as you reach all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.  
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for III days, and put on the cauterized places softened crushed with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption.  
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ingrowing flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after III days that the hair does not grow, it is good; and if those do not, repeat the cautery on those that remain from the corrupted ones. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this malady has sometimes been cured by a sharp medicine in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of the sharp medicine in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the splints which come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that by fire a sickness is born which is called “closed” according to our understanding, and it is a great thing that hinders the foot.  
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot water cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	A fire cautery is that you heat the iron as much as it is like a goose feather, and it be made of good iron to the measure that it can bend the nail on all sides, and that it have subtle margins; after that put it hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it so III days until it begins to get rot; then I make a plaster of wild mallow ground with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots.  
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place with ointment, hindering flesh until it is healthy. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring them cautery of hot water; and it is in this manner: take an iron rod or iron, or a feather of wool, and put it on the nail and the althelul, that is to say spurs warts; and put the rod so that it encompasses all around, then put a drop of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep to the root; and suffer the patient a little the biting of the hot water an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted all its roots. 
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have reached all those that are on the body, then cure the sores that generate flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling 
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make IIII cauteries or IV on the spine of the back, I cautery between each spine; and I cautery in the hip, and I on the stomach at the olive cautery; so will leave the trembling, and hasten will the saints of the cold sickness. 
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pimples 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times, by fire, the body appears with baths, or puss-filled pustules that come from large, corrupted matters.  
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at the beginning when they appear that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle stick, so that the point be seized by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or to the lentil cautery.  
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further in front, but the superfluities from which they come are removed, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.  
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut 
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great bleedings of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous thing to extend.  
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And anyway when these things happen to anyone, quickly place your index finger on the vein wound, and restrain it very much until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put on the fire olive cauteries smaller and larger as many as they are red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is closed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is restrained. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your arm above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, so take hastily another from the cautery which are on fire. 
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to make these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another evil does not come upon the patient; and know that when a vein departs from the artery, one cannot well stretch it even when the artery is great, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying of thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch the vein; and be tied and restrained carefully. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring it to rest by tightening with straps or putting hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not profit him, not at all.  
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no other remedy or medicine, he must put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is tightened over the wound and over the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it often with cold water so that it be very cold until the blood is coagulated and thickened and tightened; and make enquirings in advance those who need cauteries and medicines. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the care of stones.  
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or hot medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of the cauteries; and I have put that chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those who find it more easily what they want. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin these things, it is necessary, dear reader, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is needed.  
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.  
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have grieved themselves so much with their illness that they die easily because of the misfortune they find in their illness, and the greatness of their evil; and of these one must have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give you their sense, and say: “Wait, I am healed”; and the patient is deceitful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It does not become you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than your covetousness, and do not operate foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear friends, our Lords give you good understanding and straightness, and if you will desire to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter by chapters, according to what it is before, the chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may find them more easily those which you will need. 
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes often to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the head of the child too hard; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness except in children, and in all those that I have seen it hastened death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work for such cures. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw the child of whom the shoulder was full of water, and the head increased each day so that he could not bear it; and thought so much the moisture that he was dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the works are such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make in the middle of the head a wide incision; and be as long as II us, as long as the moisture flows; and see here the form of the spatula: 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the edges of the head open on each side, and the water flows out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you: then you must cut in the middle of the head III cuts according to this manner: 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract the moisture completely. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After you have strained the openings of linen and powders, and put wine and oil in it, and leave it so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the chief bandage be kept on, and then give the patient dry meat to avoid moisture as long as the limb is fortified and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the opening of the abscess, and the assembly of the water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess opens, and the filling of the water, and the wound according to what you have power; and guard that you do not cut the artery; and vein blood so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	of rheumatism 
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease which is called «catarrh» in the eyes or in the chest, and the illness is old, and the cure of medicine does not help at all, then the last cure is cauterization with this one which covers the two arteries. 
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you see them cover, that the patient turn back his head; after rubbing the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then stretch the patient's neck by means of the cloth; then look where the vein lies, and the ears are afterwards; then mark the veins with ink, then cut both sides with a sharp spatula from part II, until the skin reaches the bone, and this is done by the wide side of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as I do across. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood leaps out from above continuously. 
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of III digits, then seize and push until the bone; and what is due to blood to be put out is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point of the shaft, then cut that the pus does not come from an abscess, then strain the wound and tie, and the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	of migraine 
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When migraine old comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moistors of tears and the heats in the temples and ancient forehead and similar things, and it is medicated by means of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit him, if we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.  
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes backward the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned inside than in certain men who are too cold; and if it is returned, then restrain the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it upwards as pincers, and depart well from the webs that are under the skin of each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the awl, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two chiés. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all of itself at all. 
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood of the VI c., up to III; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in II lengths of a strong double silk thread, so that putrefaction may not come before the closing of the wound, and bleeding may not occur; then cut the superfluity that is between the II bindings at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize it with the cutellaire cautery up to the bone as long as the chies are cut; and this is the best work, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a warm complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is help to finish the moistors: for this cause it is of greater help to the moistors. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill their location with old cotton and put tents well made on top; and when they are loosened, be careful with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a cut of the artery as long as you work on it, then hasten to cover it with cautery, or you use the location of vitriol and strain your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don't have those present, put your finger on the location until the blood is frozen, and raise the location of cold water until the blood stops, and be strained as much as it requires; and what is more common and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenching from two parts, but the trenches be well spaced to preserve their heat for longer. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments is too hard, it holds less its heat. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one should of wide space, and then when you have signed them to the two sides, and you put the burning iron upon it as long as it comes up to the bone, and cut the vein in two sides; and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not healed from this cautery at all by any means; and this is the form of the cautery:  
des larmes	of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are above the test of the head of fur, and it does not benefit treatment of medicine one makes there, and you see the face of the patient rolling up, and feels on the forehead a walking like of trembling; and where the oil is thick and moist so that the hair of the papers falls, and the papers are dried out, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
