Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old days "bruised cure," and is that you do at the back of the patient who has this malady the hairs so that he has or front, then you make III cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II shall all remove the forehead down until the nose, and the other II along the ribs above the cheekbones, and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are at the two ribs above the cheekbones; and move your hand away from the continuity of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp on two parts of this is the form: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two incisions to all the thickness that is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second, and then extract further this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put in the first incision the instrument which is called “cultellaire”, and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the rib edge towards the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle fissure.  
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as eyes as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the one who opens the heart, and then another part do in the middle cut until the other end; and then drain the blood evenly, and press the place for the blood taken; then put in each cut a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and honey, and guard that an abscess does not come there; and on the third day untie the band, and then administer plenty of warm water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures used for wounds, as long as it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	Of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any one comes acute catarrh, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and impairing sight, and the membranes burned; and the hairs fall out, and where the head aches with a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the mother cure that is in it, so is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to retract his forehead, then make a wide cut between the eyebrows, and another one at the width of I eye. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins with the cut from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move to eat; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then dry between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow there, then cure it with drying things, that cause flesh to develop. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take II parts of flower of wheat, and of colophonia IV parts, and make a plaster; and administer it on these wounds to prevent the flesh from coming through all. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone from mine, or similar thing as iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, peas; or flowing thing such as water and wax and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, so distill any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze from condiment, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times strength comes by this cure; and if it does not come strength, then administer the extraction with fine pincers, for that is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it is possible to jump out with tweezers, that is good; if those are not possible, administer extraction to the root with a small doubleure; and if it does not come out with those, make an iron chain and put the head of the chain or ear hole strong, and plug those who are around the chain with soft wax so that the blood vessels cannot enter there with the chain; then the thread should be formed, because many times comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take a glint of what they use to catch birds, and put on some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the glint on the stone or whatever it may be, and push the thread. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all these things that we have said, then you hasten to split the ear so that an abscess comes out and spasms; and the manner of the split is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it depends; and let the cut be as a crescent, as long as you come to the bone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently with your mouth; and care for it until it is healed.  
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is in and it swells, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot issue forth, then administer the spatula gently according to this form. 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision in that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water therefore that falls into the ear, it is appropriate for the patient to use a first external dressing, and widen the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.  
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it has leaped forth by means of this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this does not work, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and easy, and warm them a little in the fire; and put them in the ear of the patient where it hurts, and lift them up with his feet on the other side, and place another stone on the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until the water comes out completely, and then let it all come out; and if you see that it does not work, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and the other end hold it in the fire until the tip of the reed is burned; then make another piece from other reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said about the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms, plug the ears, when you treat them as we said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the treatment does not help, it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun; if you see any worms, treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, take the cane of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck gently at all the ear canal; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey the order, stuff the cotton ball into the ear canal as I said in the stone. And if they do not come out further as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them treating distillations; and if distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or of lead let them be brought down to the small pores and above covered so that they can distill and in order to press from within the distillation the instrument of lead well made for this and if you see take the razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines into the cannula, and the cannula be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finishes at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside and let the distillation be a little heated by the fire so that one distills it into the ear; and keep it that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound, or by flesh born inside the ear, and these stoppages come sometimes into the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there comes I poc defuer the hole, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one, when it comes to the ear, if one cannot see it, is of grave healing in more positions, and in this one, you see that you must put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: If you see the apparent hair opening, then the work with all this spatula of this kind is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant in front and behind all plain, so that it does not weaken the ear; if the opening is of flesh or core of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ulceration is in the ear, take a fine light razor and warm it a little at the fire, then put it in the flesh of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and guard that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the puncture, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this then on no day as long as the wound is sutured, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder over pounded vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it behooves you to withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as long as it is sound. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are or treatments of distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This almond that comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and are dry, so it is necessary that you extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from its roots; then put on their place powdered vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it being decorticated, one cauterizes with the subtle lenticular cautery, and after the incision heals; and many times they return, as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return. 
de la gresle	of the groin 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem to be broken in their shape and in their hardness, and for this reason is this disease called «grainy», and it is a gathering of moisture large on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: take care if the grainy moves from one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the long way, then the peel from each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a little paper, do not worry the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, because the flesh will restore it quickly and produce cartilage. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and having the hailstone in pincers, hold the cup and press on one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hailstone is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place with that which causes char as long as the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is engendered in the tissues of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to people, and grieves much their eyes, and they come the catarrh at the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun for those reasons that the tears hasten to their eyes; and for that they lie down on their faces over, and sleep so, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist which the swelling and the appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the excoriation between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your healthy; and then take the linen drape, and arrange a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains within each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your two hands on one side and the other, so that the within be assembled between the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula a notch with a cutting edge wide, and not more than the wound that you make to the vein of the arm; and make the skin in its entirety until you arrive at the within; and in many arrangements comes within from the notch, according to the form of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove therefore a whole piece of cloth  wrapped between your two at the back, and turn your hand to right and left as much as it is spread; and guard that you do not bring in the opening, that you do not come to all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrescence does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then slightly widen the fissure until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten drapes in oil and water, and place it on top, and secure with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if to such men who grind grain and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which is lodged. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.  
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, so its cure with plasters soothing until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born adjusted other than the natural ones, and they are old, they damage the eyes, and cause kinds of illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, to the extent that it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to IV manners: or by cautery entirely fire, or by medicine aqua according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and it is made or by incision and suture or by chains, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put a needle at all the thread above; and be it beside the edge of the paper where the hair grows beside these hairs, and carry the thread upwards to all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the joined hairs, on the whole spatula, cutting from the great tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then place on top of the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is divided to all.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is to one who has need, cut a large quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then make on the whole spatula upon the II lines that you have signed, and begin with broad tears up to small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all over; then assemble the two lips at a stitch of a needle to all I thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air enter the superfluity of the filaments on both eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care of it, then leave the stitching and the threads up to III days or IIII; then cure the wound without stitching with things drying and constricting, for the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of them, but the stitching is altered (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear; and if in another manner: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, to III onions untied according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cover what goes over the small forces equally according to the form which is here. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle that has the thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put the other thread beside the large tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have marked, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canines is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make II canines by art, and II subtle ligaments as long as the paper and the breadth of the spatula are; and cut the II heads of II parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of that which overlies the paper of the eye, and restrain the II canines of the II parts forming; and let it remain so for some days, and the skin which is restrained will die and shrink and carry, until it falls off by itself.  
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if it copes with some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the II canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you pierce a fine needle, and there put the silk thread soft and fine; then join the heads and knot them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase the other silk thread finely, and tie the heads of the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy one; and be it facing the sun so that the work is clarified, because this is a subtle and fine work; then put the needle to all the chase at the root of the hair just below, and make it pierce in the paper carefully as long as you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all of the chase in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will drag the chase to the end of all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out through the opening above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will drag the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows back; and if the hairs are small, accompany the long hair of the natural horses, and raise it with that one or you leave it, as long as it is elongated and then lift it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness which is called “alegrati” or rot comes in the eye, there are two ways of it: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by suddenness of wound, or incision or cautery, and similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split that suture, and sever the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it as long as it is healing; and it is not fitting that you use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but there are works of softening things, such as fennel; and the root of water or high and linseed seeds be cooked, and oil of aquilon melted in any of the oils, and wrapped in a tent, and cure it. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you take care that it does not join again according to the form that it was before; and these works that we have said are none other than addresses of this illness, that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation is truly called “axacrati,” and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and fissure and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an needle, in which it has the double thread, and you put it in the flesh, and you make it pierce from the left lacrymal to the right, so that the threads come in the two shoulders of the flesh; then the flesh is above all the needle, and the cope at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is right, it is good; if those are not, then take the razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make II fissures where the cost is inside the paper; and let the heads of the II fissures be at the II angles of the incision that you have cut, and make such angles that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name «I griesche»; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs are added below, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the II parts severed, and the seams with a thread of linen; then cure with what we have said of softening medicines, and tents, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then carefully insert between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare everything from all their power how they make return the figure to its natural form; and the sick man himself, according to what is necessary for the operation and instruments in many dispositions.  
dou soudement de la papiere	of the swelling of the paper 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to certain people in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor do its natural works, then it becomes necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the length as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula subtle, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp nor blind the eye; and let your incision, with which you scrape that assembly, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it heals all that assembly, and no time in the eye salt water, and the rise of fresh water, and from coliere; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wool moistened in egg white; and after the third day use the coliere and things boiling until it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in II manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard syfac, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one cures panre as pinches, it cannot be undone; and both semblance commence from towards the great tearer, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head on your shoulder, then he opens his eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle at the pinches of small fold, and the top; then take a needle, and put it horse hair, or deer, or ox, and the thread strong; and double the point of the needle an inch and insert it into the angle, and pierce it to the end of the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the top; and escort all the hair the rib of the angle which follows the prunele and silk to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear to all the spatumile subtle and as small forces, and leave the flesh natureil or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears customarily; and no time is the angle at the one inch alone, and at the thread, as we have said; then the escort on all the spatumile souef from what is this the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision, put in the eye a bit of crushed silk, and with the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as it needs until it is healed.  
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not healthy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the oil for the patient, and take a light spatula sharp according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the angle above subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason is pressing, so distill from your mouth into the oil coliere made of litargire and dou coliere red and seil broiet, and stop up the eye until the other day; then begin again the other work according to this same work, as long as it is completely removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no other thing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil, then treat it with milk and first cure the boil as well as possible until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from tears harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the oncine, and in cut a part and not all at once, that body of tears does not come; then distill in the eye red coliere which is made of litargire. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the car which is born on the pupil 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red color, and cover the white and restrained on the papers and turn to the fire, and seems like a rose of balustrade; and the work is that the patient puts his head in your saint, then you operate the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable needles to those, and hold it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go all cutting to the scraper until the end, and take care that you do not blind the eye in the operation; and let the incision be like the spatula which we have said in the incision of the angle and as small forces of which one removes the sebum, as the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of seal ground or you distill red coral and similar medicines corrosive, and put on the eye fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be sure to be hot abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the without skin covers you, and you doubt hot abscess, so leave the eye and cure the abscess of things calming hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and so do until all flesh is adjusted in the eye by this likeness.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you treat the cure of each weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member be suffering from that work. 
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Those veins are red that are covered above the eye, and they take away from sight their work and weaken the eye all days.  
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that you first examine whether the eye, in which it is, is sound, and there is no other ailment except for the pupil; thus, command the patient to put his head upon your palm, then suspend those veins throughout the whole line according to your wisdom, and let the lines be subtle double according to this form:  
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two bones be joined by degrees in the body according to this form. 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then one coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see remove those veins far from the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with points of spatulas, and make this work at hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, if distill in the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the blood. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to collect all of these in that hour, make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; and this is the form of forces. 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The wound which they call «arissati» fistula: when you treat it by cautery and by medicine with fierce heat according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the craftsman has all the instruments of what here is the form; and it is called "sharp head," and be made of fiery iron to the pointed head, and be pointed like a file as much as it is in the present form:  
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on its place the broken bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little while until you know that the corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bones are fused, and flesh is born, and the body of the bow is fused, and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is not infected, know that it is healthy; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft be thinned to the chief as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it upon the bone near the tear duct, and withdraw your hand from the eye's socket, then turn all around until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the bone, then goes the matter to the cheek; so it is lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is wide open and there is no disturbance in the pupil or decrease, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then cleanse, then put suction cups or a heater without injuring for suction, then put on the eye a poultice made of acacia and aloe and frankincense and sarcocolla, and then restrain the eye, and plaster over with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind it above with a hard bandage, and start again the suction cups for suction without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye restrained day and night, and if the poultice softens, it is necessary that you restrain it very much; then remove the poultice after the day and the night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not, then start again the poultice and bandages and the poultice and suction cups until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocation of a web 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When ruptures come in the woven canvas, then open, and there comes forth pieces like grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the lower part until that above, then put another needle where it has the double thread of the tear's part; and make this pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vine around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on the other half eye, in a fold of egg white; and let it stay until the threads fall with the vine, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vine on each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, then pierce them with a subtle spatula that comes in from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and draw down the eyes, and enter into it at once; then extract it until it is healed.  
de la bowe de l’oil	of the ball of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing else but a bow which is assembled in the eye, appearing like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it as much as you see the bow coming upwards to your eyes; then be it fixed, and do not descend and let the light be unconfused, and the patient sees things as he usually does; and if it does not descend downwards, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make on the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bow is issued; and when it is issued, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that is boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the points in division, and those that are necessary to examine; so work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie his healthy eye and hold it very tightly; then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called «almagda», or with your left hand, if the eyes are right; then put the tip of the instrument next to the cornea by the width of a hair in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear duct, then thrust the instrument which is called «almagda» virtuously, and retract your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the perfect measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal fabric, and then put the instrument until where the liquid is, then squeeze it out one vein after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water now descends, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.  
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water returns up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and she does not rise, gently pull the almagda by turning your hand back and forth; and then return the water in a little bit of silk gemma, and leave that inside the eye. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of a poultice or soaked cloth with rose oil and yolk of egg, and bind with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a certain crushed thing with an abundance of egg.  
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit", of this is the form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deep in it, but make it subtly, then put in almond, as we have said; and at the accomplishment of the work equip the patient with a dorteur before, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and take light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not good that you do these things at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align these, for this reason because the water rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who assuage the abscess; and when it is appeased, then unbind the view and put on his face a little cloth to cover any day, and be in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it leaves the house little by little, and becomes in its cases; and know that no disciples must interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almond pulp, to which they added water, but all the same I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them see them; and they are of rain properly.  
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these same subtlety, and the last one in three angled sharpness. 
de la char sor le neis	of the bone about the birth 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or made various joined creatures, from which some seem scorpions with many legs; and if there are such ones where the flesh is cracked of foul color, and if there is flesh soft of good color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chariots that is sound, and not broken, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and put the oncine to those chariots, and draw them out; then cut what you can hold with the subtle sharp spatula on one part, until you know that the chariot is entirely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that one can not cover, if the one open to all with instruments subtle and light, so that it does not remain anything; and if without you summit or abscess is chosen, or secort as it is fitting; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize until the blood be stanched and be removed all the chars, then giete ou neis aisil and aigue or wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh new in the bone above, so the instruments do not come to cut: therefore, it is necessary that you put a thread of linen a little thick into it, and be bound by hands ours, and have between each knot of space one or less; and put the patient's head with the thread in his nose at its power, and pull it while smelling until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do children thus at school, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel one after the other being careful as those who are or thread.  
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the boys have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back in its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the head a bandage of cloth for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, to which one distills the oils and medicines in the head:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of iron, resembling a lamp open, like a candle, and conduct it thus; and if you see, then make a closed candle, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have the handle at the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh around the joint 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
