Many times there is born at the head of a new disease called "telul", and grows and becomes great and thick, so much that it is strange to look at; and for this it is necessary that you cut it from the beginning, and remove all bone, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, take heed if it is hard, of a dark color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron because it is an ulcerated abscess, for when one cuts it any time, it brings great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that one can cut it completely, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, because in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and incense ground together; and put over the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another kind of soldering plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.  
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the solutions: by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have let you know. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men of hands happen within the lips abscesses hard, seeming to grains of millet, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each pustule, and take with tweezers and cut in each part; then put in its place after the incision of vitriol ground, until the blood be stained; and then the leave from aisi, and cure the place of dry things until it be healed.  
de la char des gencives	of the gum 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums called "albulus"; it is necessary that you support it with forceps and cut it at its root, and leave the wound open or the blood; then put powdered vitriol or other astringent and drying powders on it; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which happens many times, cut it a second time, and cauterize it; if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of deafness 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes are assembled to the chief of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes are the teeth black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and are the teeth stinking; so it is necessary that you make sit the patient between your hands, and his cheeks be in your saint, and raise the teeth or the scabs appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do of the black and of the green, and of the jaundice and of other stains, as long as they are washed; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, so begin again to scrape the second day and the third, until you have everything scraped; and know that the teeth need diverse forms of instruments to scrape, according to that the work shows you, because the scraper with which one scrapes outside the teeth has other forms than those with which one scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to draw out as much as you can, because one must not do otherwise; for it is a substance very high until therefore one has no excuse to erase. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to take milk, it is necessary for you to be certain about the tooth aching.  
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and he thinks it is a tooth of Saint, and milk the good tooth; but nevertheless, the pain departs not by this, as long as the evil remains, because we have already seen it with these sufferers; and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, then it behooves you to scrape around the tooth at all its I. spatumile strong to ward off the gums from all parts; then move it to your two or as pincers subtle in the first hole and hole, until it is well loosened, then firmly affirm the pliers; and let the head of the patient on your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and put it gently inside each side, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it befits that you fill it with bandages where the holes are; and if it is held gently with forceps so that it does not break when it is extracted; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And thus be well warned that you do not break it, and leave a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant healers who by their haste and boldness break sometimes the cartilage, and do not bring them what we have recounted; but they cause sometimes great sickness through the opening of these, due to the roots that remain there, or through the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding comes, which often happens, apply a compress of vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one moves the teeth first, should be at long points and with wide handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:  
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the members be thick so they do not bend when working, and let them be of good iron, well made, and toothed to hold tight. 
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the teat, it is necessary that you put upon it moistened cotton with butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are swollen, put in pliers called "algefri," so that the head appears like a bird's beak; and they shall be made inside like a file, and this is the form. 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say a spatula, because this is its form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by itself, it is good; if not, then with all your instruments help, of which the forms come after here: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II reins, of this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the order of the teeth, and this instrument that seems like great pliers, whose form is here: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments are of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters clever find for themselves their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks not the bone or other bones, or he can do it, then search for the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and help with gestures, by which this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and well fitting to hold the bone, that it may not escape, but be able to hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suited to this, and if it has in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all these instruments:  
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the shape is ugly, and even in chaste women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it or sharpen it: therefore the ray; and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and resembles a small beak, and be of well-tempered iron, sharp at the top: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copy prick and prick in hand days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then file with a such as this is form: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the knife with which one makes needles; and in sharpening the edge a little here and there lightly, so that it does not move until it ceases; then the plane at the end has no trace, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to sharpen the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it to make it move without spitting, and you have cured them with astringent medicines, and this does not work; if these are needed to be restrained with a thread of gold, because the silver threads become green and rotten, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too small nor too large, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see it is necessary to adjust the teeth, then take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the cheek between the teeth, if there are one or more, until you skillfully come to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then hold the ends of the wire with pliers and assemble them, and place them between a healthy tooth and one that is broken; then tighten it as much as possible so that it does not move the tongue; and then let it remain tight for as long as it can, and if it loosens or the wires come apart, then restrain it with another wire; so it will stay and serve thus throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls, one puts it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and at times one makes the shape of a tooth from bone of bale, and puts it in the place where the deficiency is, and restrains it as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this band comes from under the tongue or nature, that it is born so; or by accident of a wound sewn; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hands, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve band wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place; and if there is stiffness or knot, and it is from the sewing of a wound, so put the probe and cut the wide ligament; and guard that the incision be not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, raise the place with rose water and ointment, or cold water; then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and dress the sick person each night, that the places may not join. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding comes, put vitriol ground on the place; and if it doesn't stop, cauterize it with the dim-sighted cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fiery color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, because it is a chancre; and if it is declining to white and there is moisture, put on an incision, and make it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the sans te goes well in your work, then put on powdered vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you extract all pus; then lift the wound of aidil and seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	At times there come from within the throat abscesses that are called “godath,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent blood loss; but leave it until it is mature, and then you will split it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color, reappear, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover it, but first look whether the abscess calms down and is appeased. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, make the patient sit facing the sun, and his shoulders be in good health, and he opens his mouth and the surgeon places the instruments between his hands, and presses the tongue down to all the instrument, this is how it is formed; and be of silver or steel as fine as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the awl and insert it into the abscess, and pull up as much as you can; and do not touch anything with the cloths, then cover the instrument, for this is the shape that seems like a force; but the head is curved, one end to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs for this is the form: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be trenchant on one side and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and so, and if a decorrement of blood happens, gargle the patient with water, or peelings of pomegranates be cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, as long as the wound is stained; then care for it until it is healed; and sometimes there are born in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them then just like the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was near inside the throat, that is to say the abscess of small sense; and I had well almost closed all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was stopped, and could not eat nor drink, and would be dead if she remained thus one day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had been driven into two furrows by its two openings. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore acted quickly, and placed one needle in one incision, then I pulled the thread out, and in the thread a great portion of pus; then I put another piece in the other point of the two, and worked the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I put the needle into these abscesses, and squeezed out a part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus the woman's throat was opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I ignited it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and know only that God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it is drawn to the eye and it is filled and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is somewhat thick and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the head of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is round gathered and is not long; and it is sanguine or of rust color or black, then it is necessary that you make a drainage incision on it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.  
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It therefore becomes necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made remembrance before; then insert the probe into the eye, and draw it out, and the cup to the II instruments that I have said in the incision of the II almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and cure it until it is healed.  
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, you should use an instrument to cauterize the senses that cause fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy side, and then he presses the tongue to the instrument we have said or chapter of cautery, and confines with very sharp gauze, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the tip of this instrument, for this reason, there is the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have or chief a hair which one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle come from his mouth of the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the neck; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it become charred and the bites of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the vein above, until the cotton is placed on the grape; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait after IV days or V And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton buttered, and purify that which is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and put it there, and boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot have the instrument heated according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be of silver or iron, and either one of the heads put into the mouth of the patient until the vapor mounts to the eye by the vein, until the eye is dead; afterwards it recommences often, until the eye dries, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen there; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a hound and put inside its head a piece of lead so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the lead does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and it is good cure altogether safe. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is lodged in the throat bone or spine of fish, or anything else; so it befits that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all your instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it befits that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by adventure it will spit out the thing with vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or the morcel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge the thread, and then swallow it again; and when it comes to its place, it will be lodged, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out with what we have said, then take the instrument of plum according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head high raised; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all does not come upon it, nor thrust in the bone inside; and moves that the patient puts out the instrument, because he will know whether it is good or the thing is difficult; so put it down, or draw it out with all the instrument evenly, as long as it is far.  
de la sansue de la gorge	of the cutting of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No times is medicine the hemorrhage, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not profit, then look at the throat of the patient to the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all little forceps, or subtle pincers that are suitable for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put fire at the end of the dog's hair, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient stands of water all day.  
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full a goblet of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he falls.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will go down without hurting him. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you light a pot where there are live coals, and let it be covered with a coverlet pierced in the middle, and in it put the head of the instrument; then you throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the sinus; and the sinus will now fall, and if it doesn't fall, then restart the fumigation many times; and endure the patient thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then there is need that it be gone by this governance. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument for treating the throat, is when it can be seen, resembles curved pliers to enter into the throat; and has the semblance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness of lime, so that whoever takes it, it cannot leave; and see here the form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many types of abscesses are, according to what remembrance comes here after from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in II ways which one is in its own likeness, and of that which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs where they are in the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an abscess one should not pierce until the bow is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if some such that it behooves to pierce when they are mature and do not die according to their fulfillment, as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it be as long as it is rotten, by chance the ligaments and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is a cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When an abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay piercing it until it is mature, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the base, pierce it so that it is mature; and it is not good that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for the one that is near the base, that it may not go too far, and be elongated inside, and a fistula comes; and it cannot heal in a great term. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and of the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it is more dependent from the abscess, and where it appears ripe; and let the perforation be long of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no pleurisy.  
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that are dislocated, according to the member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the puncture open as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce him before those things, then the body of the venom will lengthen from him, and it is full of much filth; and by chance hardens the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess which are perceived according to the breadth of the body, according to what the members have need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the core, and cover; when it has become as I drapes, and is softened, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are split in III angles, and if there are such that one cuts like the myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the armpits; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other sizes and appearing cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Whoever does not have a head, such as a superficial boil, it is necessary that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then stop the abscess until the other day, then do not drain anything; do this many times from great to great, until the pus is all out; same for if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit.   
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes bursts forth with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you are not worried about it. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, so wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, administer bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have stitched it together, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shred of linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then dissect it, and treat it with ointment as long as it is healing. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the flow of blood happens in your work, so administer cold water and ease it, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter's time, and the place or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it is fitting, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the cures of abscesses: for I have told you how one must go before the cures of abscesses, and see here the chapter.  
des soros	of sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where boils on the head come small abscesses, and they are manners of ours that are in cloths, as the joiner of a hinge, and there are many similarities. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and such which have moisture like pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the hip are such that you should consider all instruments which are called "entromissoire," because their form comes here afterwards, what they contain. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so lift it from above with a long stick.  
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried up, then carefully remove without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns back if you leave it there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and honey, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and cover those which are left over with nit. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the nit; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it be healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, cut it according to this form, long; and put your needles there, and the peel from all sides, and put all your care to drain the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterward. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is purulent, and with cutting and caring as I have told you.  
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting above the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and from these old abscesses that I treated or chiefs of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had made any incision in it, one would have done as well a wound as with a stone.  
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, it is that which come to the chief of children and to the roots of ears, the opening so be always at the lowest point, in order to better drain the boil; and treat as it befits. 
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous ulcers 
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come in other parts or of the body, and are bad, and are joined together with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its side, as the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.  
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that one therefore that you see of good disposition at the touch, and seems like to the color of the body, and mute of each part and is not a bit averse as the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; then it is fitting that you cut it from above, and the peel of each part, and are the II lips of the heart as onions, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the treat prick and prick, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and be not too spatumile or trenching, that the hands do not escape, and do not see too ahead, that you do not cut those that you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, so put in the wound vitriol ground, or any powders that restrain blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then examine with your index finger if there are any small pustules remaining, if so cut them and grind them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is in the root of the scrofula a vein great, then it does not behoove that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it without annoyance; then apply to the wound old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then that there is no longer any superfluity for the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk the juice, and the count as we have said.  
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce there where it appears moist; and pierce it like the one said before, depending on it, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply ointment to cure the flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of dislocation 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have squinance, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called «epiglottis» be eschewed; and one does not make aid by this, because all the veins and li pormon dou malaide are to those who have abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in II amandres. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It befits then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV with a small slit through, between the II circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and this is as suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long of equal length. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it behoves him to extend the skin of the throat to all the neck, then split the keel until it comes to the windpipe; and shut off the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe which is ejected from the place that is broken, and by the absence of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.   
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is past because of which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew together alone along the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the lung.  
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to stitch the wound and care for it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to cure her, and found her as dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and knew well that it had not been cut vein nor led forward except to the throat, and the veins flowed through the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it and thus I cured the wound until it was healed; and the young lady did not feel anything but that her voice was hoarse, and she returned afterwards to her disposition; for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a wound, and it is mostly in women; and it is according to two ways: natural, and accidental; where naturally there is no instrument. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat us, and the other manner is similar to abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not agree to work to do outside than in that which is small, and prove and search throughout the intruder: if you find him as I fat, and cannot at any vein, so cut it, as one cuts the ours, and treat all its head, if there is any; and surround well then, and cure it as it befits, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all appearances; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and outcome. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is sometimes accompanied by fever, as long as the boiling is passed and the putrefaction is complete, then the fever and heat subside. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one it has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the syfac, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a bruise, and becomes big; and they are according to two appearances, or fat, or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this type of ailment, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to its shape and chapter which is after.  
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of probing abscesses in our way is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it is according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care in what falls out.   
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs short, whatever its color, treat it as I have said about other abscesses; and if after the probe moisture does not come, know that it is fatty, so treat it in a cross, and take it with pincers, and gently scrape each side and ward off the coat where it lies that you may draw it out sound with the [hand]; and if you cannot draw it out sound, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a bit, and the skin does not grieve, then employ the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and restrain the wound, and put upon it soothing things, an abscess hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the swelling is great, then sew the two lips of the wound, and cure it from those who form flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is beating against you it is contrary or another haste and employ the place of vitriol ground, and let it lie II days or III, as long as the wound rots, and rest the boiling of blood; then return to cover what remains from the new. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the intromittent instruments, and they are of III ways: great, medium, and small; and there are III squares which are called "albaret," and I which is called "breb," and there are of III ways: great, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews clothes, and they are of citrine brass, or iron, or silver, and the most valuable are those that are yellow, and they are more proven of black bronze to encircle the edges of fistulas; and they are of III ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the  scalpels are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are scalpels that have two curves in three ways also; and there are scalpels that have three curves, and are also in three ways; and there are scalpels that have two curves, and scalpels of one curve only, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these are what one makes, cutting, and some there are that do not cut at all except from one side, with which one scrapes the flesh, for this reason one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and of these intromittors are the alemeles put in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and flanks, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, seeming like scrapes of fists, according to this form, for which one drains blood.  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And place it once at its place which is safe from cutting of the veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like women's breasts; and remain deformed and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it must be done according to this form from this line b. up to g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound to prevent it from festering, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the woman's breast sags down, and softens due to its size as women have, make two incisions in two ribs above, by two similar cuts; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply there what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary for healing, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made entirely because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it there until it softens the remaining part and the fat, then cure it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks  
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas that have ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture it behoves that they be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.
