Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and cure with ointment thereafter as long as it heals. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulous sores, then treat it as we said for cutting into scrofulous sores, and if the wound is hollow inward, apply cautery as we said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin above is sewn together, many times abscesses occur; and it also happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if one knows this is from the artery, then the abscess becomes long because of it; and when you feel it with your hand, you feel the constriction; and when it is from the vein, it feels like a burning appearance; and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the arms and in the groin and neck and many other places, and it is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron cure, and in those that are at the head, it is also necessary to avoid it, and in those who are inflamed of arteries by making through the skin with a long incision; then work the size as usual, and depart beautifully the artery from the tissues, as long as it is uncovered; then put under it a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries which are in the temples; then point the place that is between the II ties of an intromissoire as long as the pus that is there comes out, and let the abscess be clean; then administer the cure that is caused by bowing, until the thread falls; then cure with ointment coming after these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have I double thread, so that you lead it to the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or join of one of II parts as II chiés of thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issuing, put another needle to all I thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in IIII leagues; then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then put on top I drapeil moistened with wine and oil, then administer them cures of tents and ointments as long as it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves  
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are burnt or by too much work, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all the parts where there are joints, and it is a grief of abscesses, and its color seems the color of the body, and is in more dispositions without pain; and when one restrains it, the patient feels pain, and is not well from the whole body, but below the heart; and it moves well on all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go into contraction; and that which is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin to the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, then suspend it with a thread, and scrape it, then clean out the pus and stitch together the wound, and care for it until it is healed.  
des grosses boces pendans	of large swellings hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and are the roots subtle, and the head large; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had II in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had fine roots, and they were slightly cut, and moist from within. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision so that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artiful is white and moist and of subtle root; if the cope to the spatula large, and be in your presence the cautery at fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the hip many times there come very great hemorrhages of blood, and if the patient is healthy, then haste then to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, take a thread of good silk, and bind it as we have said, and let it be for a day; and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of silk until it cuts the artery, and closes by itself without labor; and if the roots are thick, you should fear to cut them all at once because of the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the part which is of a dull color and poor sensation and has a milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the cure of the ulcer afterwards. 
quant li boude ist fuer	When the tumor has increased 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other sores, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is from the rupture of the skin and the issue of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with diverse issue. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its sides, it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look at its appearance whether it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.  
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So it is necessary that you leave the care. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be extended straight, then reign around the entire bowel; then command him to seize his belly between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the whole great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a very strong silk cord firmly, and let it be tied together with both ends tied; then operate on the half of the abscess extended upon the thread, and put your index finger into it, and try the intestine; if you find it held by the thread, then untie it, and bring the intestine out from the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery or vein opposes you, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross as you make it perceivable; then strain the abscess on four places above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place until it dries, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and dried, then cure it according to what is necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place according to what is necessary, and weld the place. 
dou chancre	of the ulcer 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one must work on it with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say the chancre begins in the marshes, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where one can erase it like a chancre which is in the breast, and in the groin, and in similar places, and one must remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never been able to cure any, nor has anyone else ever cured me before. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge once the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion; then make the patient lie in a good position to do the work; then give your incisions or ulcers, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything; and leave to drain the blood completely, and hold well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the flow of blood goes against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it as long as the blood is extinguished; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.  
de ydropisie	of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is lit only; and one must not touch iron in these II similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hypoarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as thirst and solution of belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: lift the patient straight on your hands, and the ministers press the belly by putting the water to the lowest part of the loin, then take the spatula according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenches of II parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	To the point, and carefully not so far in that it could reach the intestine when inserted, and do not let it bleed; then see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must cut into it on the right side of the belly three fingers below the nipple; and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then make your incision on the left side of the belly three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, then make it on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to that weak place; then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and insert it, and raise your hand across the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or a little more; then pierce the syfac until the spatula reaches the point where it is eight fingers deep, and this is the place for the water, then draw out the liquid, and insert this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, and it is of iron or archut light, and in the part below there is I small hole; and where it costs on one side, III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and that is the shape of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather:  
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top above is the ailment, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it draws it now onto the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than what is right in that hour, by chance the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick person signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is retained now by the heart which stops the opening which is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument again the other day, if you see the patient suffering so, and treat from the liquid a small quantity; do this any day, and keep yourself from foolishing as long as there remains but an ounce of liquid. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you put much water on him, cure him with earth or sand that is warm, and with much sweat or bath and sun, and make him drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no holes in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If this is necessary, then he must quickly be able to pierce all with a very fine spatula according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put in its place the small thin cloth of lead, and tie it and keep it so for three or four days and when he wants to urinate, have the cloth removed, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The one whose hole is small, if it is medicated with the clo of flint as we have said, it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the penis in its place are pale, because none are born with the penis at the head of the shaft, which is why they cannot urinate before raising their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the semen cannot come to the glans, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies down on his back, then are the head of the staff and the cup as much as the width of a feather, so that the point falls in the middle, as it ought; and keep yourself from the flow of blood which often comes, and if it happens, with the sponge of those who sponge blood, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albathe comes to the rod, and is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant; so it behooves you to prick them with the fine needle, and cut and clean all of them, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.  
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is bad, of foul color and pus-filled, then you must bring a cautery to it.  
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the bone is in some the shaft, and in part inside the skin and part outside, then it befits that you remove the bone which is inside first; and when it is joined, then cure the outside.  
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, make sure the head of the rod is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its rod and groin; so it is necessary to shave all that is black and corrupted, then lay on top the plaster of honey and flour made from bark of crab apples and ivy, then cure it with other dressings until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways: that is to say, for the removal of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must put or lead from the penis a chain of plank, and piss the patient among; and when the skin is raw at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the sharp instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is a painful thing to devise this, it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any notch from the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate them between two, and put the fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not become raw. 
de la circoncision	of the circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of healing; however, when we perform this operation by our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest to heal. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the most part of masters and surgeons who did circumcisions near the Dale, and with forces, and with a whole scalpel; so were their shears because there are two cloths, and by chance if one cuts above and leaves below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the repair is necessary, and the pain doubles, and in the purification that is done with salt, the tip of the limb is not assured; and in the purification of the elbow by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times it happens that they are born like this and they do not need purification and I have wanted it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made by force to the whole line of filament I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, equally sized in all parts, and hold; but that the strands be well placed within the skin; and so the manner of the first operation is that you make the child think, if he hears, that you are only tying the strand around the rod just so, and then let him go in all ways that you can; then make him stay between your hands straight, and place forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the rod and blow or heart, and draw it up until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below I one to the other thread; and hold as II should by the second link to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the II links; then lift the heart upwards gently and draw the head of the rod; then let the blood come out little by little, for that is the healing; and put powder above and above the powder, I drape with a cloth of a cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, confectioned with rose oil good and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and treat from another cure as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the mounding is this: the two shoulders should be held and sharpened, and the shoulders should be as large as the hands equally.  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the hairs inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the hairs make an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they last III days, and what is below the penis is swollen, let it be until the abscess heals, and the skin is lightly scraped; then cut it as you can move it, and keep away from the part of the penis, it will not harm him anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place with things soft wound of powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one strikes on the heart excessively, and it goes above, so will not harm; cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	holding back of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the bladder or neck, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above his back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", of which this is the form: and be of subtle silver light shaft, like the feather of a bird; and be the cane half a palm long, and be subtle at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the discharge of urine is that you take the double thread, and tie it to the head of the wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis from above towards the bud; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient coming to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that because the conductor or where it goes is twisted; then stay the thread at all the wool head and head, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and make correction of the urine; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or there is rot assembled there, and you see them distill liquids and medicine, then do to all the instrument that is called “clepsedre,” and this is its form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leaves of the medicine should be such that it well stops the rod without addition, so that if one can draw out the moisture, and put back when necessary; and when you see putting your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the tube in the moisture, and draw with the tube which is inside; so draw the moisture into the tube, and then push back the tube firmly inside; thus will enter the moisture inside, and it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: so it is here: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of wood, and the head is higher; and below to the breast where the bones lie; then take a bladder of sheep and put in it the moisture which you see to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a double thick thread, and heat the part of that moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the shaft, then press your hand on the bladder at all the moisture coming, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it round, and pierce it through and through; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles a hoop, and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work of size; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell it to you openly and briefly.  
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is found in the bladder more often happens to children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it opens up the urethra, and makes the patient's penis heavy, and it pricks many times, and then softens; and with many of these jumps the foundations are made; and it is light the cure of children until they have IV years, and it is very severe in the elderly, and is as much as those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter from those who have large stones, than from those who have small. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the mucus that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not come back up; then make him sit between your hands well supported, and his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined down; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then haste now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at touching all, then moisten your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is young, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your right hand, push it toward the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your right hand, and put it out to where you want to cut.  
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part where one makes the incision; then he puts the spatula cutting, because this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be right above the stone, and the two sides be even or foundation, and let the waist be traversed so that it is wide outwardly, and inwardly narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large; perhaps the press on the two which is or foundation, that she jump out without labor; and know that there are such stones which have angles, and margins: if it is grieved to issue; and if to one which is smooth, seeming a gland, and round, whose issue is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To him then where there are angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you extract it with pliers which are also like a file at the head, in order to force the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under the I subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the hole of the passage, and if the stone does not come out, extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then draw the stone forth, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sewn up, and a larger wound must be made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes back through where the veins cannot join; but all the same, you try to drain it, or to cut it with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have finished your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top a soft cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reduce it, then arise well its place of oil and water, then the cure of diaphynicon ointment and basilum ointment, until it be healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this retention the urine, which is known in such manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore, put all in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it; then lift the wound of water and ease and of silk, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is found in the urethra, and is caught there, and the urine cannot pass; so the cure of those things as I say now, that you cut it many times, and are excused from the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take one piece of iron in this form, and let it be shaped like three angles fastened to one stick. 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then thrust the forest into the shaft lightly, as long as it reaches the stone; and turn the forest in your hand on the stone point by point, until you can feel the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then broken, and thrown out with the urine, and the patient heals; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and the other above, then make the rod go into the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens sometimes that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens once, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who reveals herself to the eyes, even when she is chaste.  
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, so it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity arises to this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and at pains find one, and if you do not find one, point to desire I cast mire subtle; and present her a bail well wise in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her that she does what you command of the inquisicion of the stone; and regard well whether the woman is virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her buttocks or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she constrains it below her buttocks, and recommends to her that she put her buttocks or with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder form.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it behooves her to move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the cone, where it is seen to appear and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its back above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small; then put the head into the waist, if you feel the stone so near the wound as much as the stone can exit, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound is not closed, put crushed vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the wound is stitched up; then return to your work, as long as the stone is present, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones for men so that they can help you in your work; and if the wound does not close, and it is an artery that is cut, put powder on the site and bandage it with bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not operate on it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the parts are dried, return to your work, as long as the stone remains in place. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the yolk of the eggs, that contains the egg; and it is called “syfac,” and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have said; and these have no such thing.  
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is of weakness that comes from the genitals, and that matter is spread.  
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the buttocks, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is re-formed, I see long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the buttocks, because it has moisture all around.  
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, so is the abscess re-healed with a piece of the egg, and for that reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then it feels well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, you suspect at all the intromissoire quarreit, of which the form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then which comes after the introducer, judge of what is within. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him many cloths; then sit on his left side, and command the minister that he sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the sides; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the sides among them long until near the nipple, and let your incision be straight dividing the skin of the sides up to the white fat, and the scar carefully according to your strength; then pierce the white fat full of water at the large opening, and extract all the water, and then put your compresses, and stretch the white fat upwards; and do not touch the heart of the sides, but only the white fat; cut all or in pieces equally the side of him carefully, that if you do not cut it well wisely, it will return the water; and if the bone was in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white fat; then join the two leaves of the heart of the sides with a suture, then cure it as other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the outpouring of blood; then cut the cone to all the suspended part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you did the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound lint moistened in rose oil; and put outside another lint moistened in wine and oil, and place it on top of the two pads, and put a double cloth on top, and bind it with all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two bandages, and use them of wool padding according to this semblance, and be assembled by sewing in the groin of the breeches, and one of the arms pricks on the foundation up to the back, and the other to the part of the armpit; and the other two chief over the two shoulders, and let the whole restraint be assembled in the buckle of the breeches; and sometimes is medicine this ramice of cautery instead of a size of iron, and it is that you prick the cautery knife-like fine, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be scalded as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at the once, and scorch it with this fine hot cautery. 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cap in all ways that you can, as long as you scratch everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saving; and move guarding against a decrease of blood, and moves that the works of size; and if nothing makes contrary to you, or abscess chaus or a decrease of blood or other thing, so cure what makes contrary to you, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, administer a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the watery root is there, so make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with all the spatula wide, and put the perforation long of the body; and let the openings be wide, so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave for the remaining water to run out, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then you should put in a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which the form is before; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and so the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, therefore it seems to me that one should leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess.  
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; and this is due to many causes. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and aguish, which is spread to the groin, or percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a painful abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grievous, fearful and stony, and of dusky color, and sometimes comes from without an artery, or inflammation of a vein.  
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by means of an artery, then it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not necessary that you touch it.  
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the inflation of a vein is known by its disposition to the feeling of the fingers, and one can well do the cutting on this likeness, and on the other charters; and it is that you cut out the kernel of the coins, when the egg is above, and the white side of it forward, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg.  
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cooked with these needles, then you must pull out the egg, and cut it; and if it is raw in the yolk or in what is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all that membrane, and cut it roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or their rear, then you must cut it all out and extract the egg, as we have said.  
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are completed, so apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin  
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a boil enclosed in an envelope similar to the onion, with the softening of the contents, and the patient cries out when it goes; and the cure for this disease is as frightening as the one before, but nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the raised seat, then put the suspensory of the reins down to their hips, over all the vessels which are near the penis, and have the masters tie them, and extend them; then cut with a sharp trowel wide through the middle of the vessels, so that they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples; then put a needle where the vein has come, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as with others where you want to avoid a boil, so that no vessel should be cut that nourishes one of the reins; for by this there comes no evil, and if blood comes to all the vessels, it is necessary to draw blood from all the vessels; so that the penis does not lose its nourishment for the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot help itself.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh  
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this limb are by the section that comes or syfac, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either of the syfac, or of the extension of it, and come these II manners of mouth of causes: or percussion, or jump, or braire, or lifting of heavy load, and by similar things; and the signs when it is of the extension of the syfac, are that they have poc and poc, in long time, and do not come suddenly; and are the abscesses even until toward the parfont, for which the syfac presses the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the sifac, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and are the abscesses diverse appearing, under the skin near, and it is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the sifac. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are trapped with the bowels, and held in there, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
