Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron fear, for which it is necessary to avoid it. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to put their intestine into their hand within the wound, if it can enter; then be situated upon his neck, between your hands, and lift his hips; then keep the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin long; then put into the spaces of the waist probes according to what you need for opening the wound, and let it be such that blood may issue from it; then scrape the soft tissue that is under the skin of the groin, until the white soft tissue on all sides is uncovered; then put your index finger in the one that follows the groin, in the one which is between the white soft tissue that is under the skin of the belly, and the second soft tissue, and depart from the one behind the belly, and between the second soft tissue; and then move with the right hand inside the heart of the groin, and keep the white soft tissue on top to your left hand, and lift the belly to all the soft tissue toward the waist; and command the minister that he extend the belly up, and untie what is behind the ligament; and look with your fingers if there is any intestine enveloped or white soft tissue hard, and if you find any of these things, put it in the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it into the back part of the soft tissue, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the heads that appear from the threads, as long as there are IV threads; then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the soft tissue, of which we have said that it is under the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then envelop the heads of the threads, and tie them together from II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish it may enter inside, except an abscess may come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread of II parts, and after these II threads leave the soft tissue that is under the heart of the groin the greatest of a part; and after all the other one according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the groin, as long as the sinew and the bow, as we have said before; then administer moist wool in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put in the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the whites (as we have said), after the incision, for fear of  discharge of blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the bond until it dries per him; and if it is late in drying, let it be rinsed with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with other cures, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancient ones said that it is made like the branch which is together with the vein, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut it in half, and cure the abscess of those who work, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the bowels, as we have said, and opens the limbs; and do not insert any of the entrails into the bowels, and if there are any inserted, it is little, and repairs all hours; and nonetheless, if it remains too long in this point, it believes the wound or the abscess, as long as the intestine exits; and this happens because of the extension of the abscess which is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is extended, then it softens and swells the limbs and opens; and the cure is thus by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies wholly on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated from the width according to the quantity of III does; and then extract the abscess which is below the skin that the usual, then take the thread and put it on the place appearing of the abscess; and press it in the front part of the belly, then sew the II places appearing of the abscess above the head of the thread, and sew one and the other; then extract the head of the thread, and do not cut the abscess nor extend the gut or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The incision is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and closer to salvation. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals  
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the contents within them are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to heal it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and the cut the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread. 
dou chastrement	Through chastisement 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisement is common in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two ways: one of which is that the wise man knows how to answer when asked, and knows the cure; and the other, because we often need chastisement from some beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and oxen and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that treatments are done according to two ways: or by attraction, or by fending. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by traction, let the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and pliable; then grasp them with your hand until they are set back and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of the tail: it behooves you to hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut above each testicle at one go, when you will have well scraped them; and let no prickle remain of the syfac and the subtle syfac which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is more effective than that done by attraction, because in attraction, perhaps nothing remains from the testicles, for which reason the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as men: the one if it is that between the two sexes opens as much as the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in court the urine. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and it is on the pointed part as well as a rod, and they will conceive. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of man and woman is that you cauterize all attached boils, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of their genitals, there is no treatment. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a char attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tissue with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not pull too forcefully, lest bleeding occurs. Then treat the wound after another cure until it is healed; and to another char which arises at the mouth of the marsh, and the armpit, and by chance may be, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "the disease of the cow".  
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the treatment, and the cure until it is healed.  
de erratique	of wandering 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by illness that came to it; or it is because of a char adjusted, or through subtle or thick syfac, and it is made in the groin, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and possibly flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the bailiff.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is appearing close by, if you want to [place it] on either side or to the back. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is with subtle forceps, and it is near the two books, then hasten, and do thus: put your two finger indices together, and let the woman be on her back, legs spread; then extend the two books so that the subtle forceps are round, and over the stupefactions; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lie the woman flat each day, so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the stylus is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with the spatula seeming to a myrtle leaf.  
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppage is of flesh, then suspend it at the hinge and the cup; and have the medicines stanching blood, as for example, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with a handful of egg; then administer a poultice of broad plantain, so that the wound may not close; and thus be long, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other cures until it is healed.  
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a new birth, it is necessary to cover according to this manner, if it is not abscesses inflamed. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is inflamed which is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without custom, become hardened; and when hemorrhoids are old they become like thread; and we have said in the division their resemblances, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve healing. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are inflamed in the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, except for by iron.  
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then after the altar has been taken with tongs, and the root cut, then powder of medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and aisil, and make a plaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he strains, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it does not, apply a suction cup to the back and breasts without harming them; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply a poultice there. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the sharp chief, so it must be covered as I have said the thelul; and then the cure until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marshes 
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marsh, such as boils and cancerous abscesses and herpe and styes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the groin, which is not like the abscesses that boil over; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see whether the abscess is thick at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but allow him to rest until the pain is appeased; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and let him have small seats where he can recline, and lean against his back and assemble his legs to the outside of the thigh; and let his hips be spread out, and place his arms below his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then lift him toward the right side, and there administer the instrument which is used for opening the mouth of the throat, so that as it comes after the form; and it is necessary when you see to administer this instrument, that you put the end first in order to know the depth of the throat, so that what goes into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the throat with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and let him put the cone of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with the hand, then it is necessary to cover it on the head, with the spatula laid; and when the wound is empty, it is necessary that you put into the wound damp wads in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the wad from the wound to the edge of the margin, and put outside over the margin and over the bandage linen clean moistened in water or mallows boiled; then cure after II days of ointment preceding this, until it is healed; and at no time raise the margin and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and agrimony long boiled; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in its place, then you should guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.  
de l’enfantement	of childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman hasten downward, and desire to smell the air; then the child hastens by force to issue forth; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the head first, and the buttocks with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary gently press her belly so that the child issues forth soon; for when it comes upon its head, then the buttocks are with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes on his feet, and comes forward the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes on his belly, or groin, and is converted by chance on his neck, and other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the healer that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.  
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural birth, and the woman labors hard, and the virtue of her is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the small spatula whose form is here between her buttocks: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cleave the secondine and cut to its nail as long as the moisture which is in it comes out; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her suck and sneeze with condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus now will come the child. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you put them gently back and forth; and if they cannot go in, then place the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up; then tilt the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the tilting; and if the hands cannot go in, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the neck which is put before this, and extract the child, and reset it evenly.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn it back and forth, until it is equal; then grasp its feet and extend them back and forth.  
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Unless he jumps to his hips, as commanded, then take him, and let him sneeze from the condition; if he sneezes, may God help him. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not good as we have said, so turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore then there is lightly. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have, say to take a mustilage of aloe, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until below the ribs; and when she is softened below, then make her the collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and take her belly gently, because now the child jumps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands on his breast, and then they are positioned on his neck, and the feet hang down. And he lies on his bed, and folds his hands on his breast, and then takes his hands over his stomach, and takes away the cushions beneath until she is prepared downward; and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them forward, then moves his stomach up, then pushes with his hands; and thus the child back and forth; and commands the woman to hold herself as long as the child comes. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out with a hand wide 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to attempt to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, have the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie down on her bed, and straighten her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and when the child is born according to its natural figure, make her sneeze and command her to hold it until the babe is out. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned toward the back of his mother 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bailiff holds his hand, then turns it little by little and lightly; and when it is aligned, he puts on the muscle padding of elevation and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to hold; and the woman sneezes.   
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the spine 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner to the whole secondine, so cut the secondine at your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; and if the infant can hold up on his face and on his neck, so cut from under the hood that it does not remain held, and kill the infant; then put the child inside, until you have placed him as it should be, and command to the woman that she should not touch it at all times; therefore, it will come out more easily. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often.  
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they are named; I know those, that they be multiplied, and are divided by the syfac which devises them, which is joined to the head; and sometimes go out as naturally as all under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they stick out sharply, so the cure as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do thus as he is fit to heal. 
de plusors enfans	of many children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all these, because by chance something similar happens to them; so it is done according to what is necessary.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands; so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; so it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her shoulders inclined down, and the legs raised; and the minister holds her by two parts, or she is bound to the bed so that she does not move in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with moss of altee and fenugrec and seed of flax, then anoint the hands of her with these oils and these muscillaiges; then put them into the womb gently, then try the place where she puts the pins that are convenient to those, and take ward if the child is appeared that it descends upon its head; so put the pins in her eyes or her neck or her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on feet, so put them in the thigh and at the middle ribs; and it is necessary that he holds the pin with his right hand, and puts the curve between his two of the left hand, and he puts it to all his hand gently, and puts the pin in any one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them equal in moving from one side to the other, so they can move easily, and let the bones have teeth so they can hold, as this is the form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains, he anoints the bail with oil from one of his eyes, and puts it in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remains, he places this (oncine) or higher up, and does this until it comes out entirely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, it is necessary that you envelop it on the drape, until it is whole; then cut in the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and thus you must do in the other hand, and as for II feet.  
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is protruding at the birth canal, where there is a sharp chief assembled, then you should put the pointed spatula between your two fingers, and make the chief and extract the sharpness; or you can use the instrument which is called "almidach", so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head goes back and is forced, then split it, until the moisture which is or worse exits; and if it cannot exit, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is inflamed in the belly or below the ribs, then you should pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the mare is light.  
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is a strangulation in the belly or the breast, then it behoves you to draw it out with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is there corrects; and if the other members are outside, and the head remains, then push the bail your hand into the marrow, and drag it to the mouth of the marrow; then he pushes in the pin or two, and drags further; and if the mouth of the marrow is contracted by a boil that has come, then it does not behoove to work it, but rather things moist and fatty must be administered; and administer plasters, and sicca in mollifying and moistening water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, so administer what we have said in the living child; and if one has no power, then the body should be treated in pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you will have done this, if it is administered to those that we have said about abscesses which come in the marshes; and if the flow of blood comes, be put in astringent water, and administer other treatments. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been dead, then she conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.  
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time he came to have an abscess on his head, and it swelled so much that it opened and began to discharge pus greatly.  
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long time, and could not solder the wound. 
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong traction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.  
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much amazed, because this one whose belly has no bones. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound, and in tracing my hands over the bones, as long as the woman was in better condition; and visited the woman a long time then, and she would come back to a little bit of swelling in that place; and I haven't recorded this chapter for any other reason than because when the masters find a strange thing, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here after comes the form of the presser, to what one is given the books; and its turning as its two arms of its two members.  
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the tube I must be wide, and the edge of the trees it must be, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same tube, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the clamp to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	One other form, in appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pliers; and has two jaws with adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and two wide; and when you see opening the vagina with the entire instrument, then have the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then put the two jaws together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument as you have done with pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the woman does what she wants.  
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all mounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the one sees them appeared, so much is more haste in the work, and higher to men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the tool that you may have prepared it, because their necessities are not excusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you order the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well done. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not so, take a pot and make it perforated or covered, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be boiled or put in water on the fire; then put a chain or perforated lid on the pot, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and hold it until the vapors come from within the marsh; then make him sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the back of the hip jumps suddenly.  
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the midwife to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in althea musk, and then put it into the womb, and hold it there; and when she finds it, grip it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the thread does not fall away during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; and it will come and disengage. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare is narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not use the milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then the clisterize of ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it will bear and put back, and will come further; but nonetheless, when she bears it so there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and pales the sick. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is appropriate for fumigations suitable to these: none of the ancients have experimented with fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and of the second is this.  
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to see as a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire; and let the fumigate be over the embers, and the tar until it is burned, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without the base pierced, but with a subtle sty: so it befits the midwife to pierce that sty in its place, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard the lacement so that she does not touch it; then put a soft cloth moistened in wine and oil, then the ointment of cure until it is healed.  
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will return, then put or place a piece of wood, and leave them hands for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into rooms. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stupefaction comes from the swelling of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that swelling; if it is cured, as we have said of the cauldron of lead.  
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation 
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and still moisture attracts white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and they are known by those who have them by ejection or flatulence when the patient expels, and by chance in jumps a few.  
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if to fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to the half of the penis; and reach to the junction of the hip, and to the buttock. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula by piercing at the base, and not piercing: and it is that you put your finger or foundation, and put a fine needle of iron or steel in the fistula when there is no twist.  
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twistings, then put in a tent of fine wool, or horsehair, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no discharge through the opening nor venting nor liquid, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure it.  
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be stopped by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced to the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes to the place; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around, then it is that it is adés bowe, and it does not worth medicine nor treatment by ointment; and in these fistulas piercing has no cure other than labor, and vanity of the foolish miracles who intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is neither too young nor too old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you raise his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly; then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, you should put your index finger there, so that you feel when it touches; and be discovered whether you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then know that it is pierced; if it doesn’t work at all, one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One must nevertheless say that one can heal some well, but this happens little; and the help that one does is to carefully sharpen the cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and put it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches the bottom; and do this II times or III, as long as you know that these fatty charcoals are burned, which resemble an eye feather; and then cure with damp bandages in butter, until those charcoal is gone, then cure with ointment sealing and binding. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, that is well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, it cannot be healed in any other way; and if it sticks between [things] and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your two parts and the tent a thick covering of flesh or syfac, and you see the fistula at the end of the covering as follows, then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the tent, and after that apply the cautery until it reaches the top of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and fall off; then remove those charn that appear like a feather of an owl, and nothing remains.  
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound festers, and it comes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of those joined bones, and the quenching of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of moist tents in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the wound lies low, and there are the burned bones in the hollow; then cure the wounds of sudden openings encasing hard bone, and they are the dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.  
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to right through the bottom of it, and is separated from the body, then you cut it at its base or foundation, and ask about those. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there between is the web or the syfac or chars, where it is close to piercing, if there is no other way except by faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents and cure as first; and do not let it too much in parfont, so that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and come the egestions by the lay will; then the cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound once it is cut from its base, or by tent or by another pointed instrument; then munde the char fautree who is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: this will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the base near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts the thread wrongly into the second, and pushes the tent all along the thread into the fistula until it is at the head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you push your fist or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two ends together, and restrain them to each other, and leave it one day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads heal those cars which are between two, and stick; then cure the wound until it is sutured and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a bandage cover them if they are pierced, and then treat them, as we have said, until they are healthy. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinal scapula from which one makes the fistula is very narrow on one side and trenching; and on the other side no, because for that reason one does not cut where one should not cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids 
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, they contain blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those which are outside have little moisture, and it contains a little bit of clear water or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation is that you command the patient to stretch out to go into rooms, until the foundations come out, and the filaments appear; then hasten, and you can hold it with tweezers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the pincers cannot hold it because of its moisture, take it with a drape, or cotton, or a piece of felt; and extract it to your fingers, then cut it, and powder some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cautery; then cure the other cures until he is healed; and if the foundations cannot come out, clench the patient with a mordant and harsh enema to wash what is in the foundation so that it can come out clearly; as long as the patient takes care, and if his filaments are outside the foundation, the cure is easy; and it is that you grasp them with your finger or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until he is healed, and that he fears incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take I thread and put it into a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so be wide; and tighten the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do likewise for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation I drapery moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave him until they are dry, and when they will be dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until he is healed.  
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of humors within the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not work.  
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not leave it moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should; and if it cannot heal, begin scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then treat it until it is cured.  
dou fremit	Of trembling 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formic is a small appearance of fault before the body, and it goes much in them; and sometimes she finds it cold, and feels it like death of trembling, and comes to the whole body, and more to the hands than another part.  
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cauterizing iron from a goose feather, or a vulture’s feather very strong, and put that cauterizing iron on the sore, until the purple circles encircle the sore all around; then turn your hand all around the cauterizing iron until you cut all around the sore, and put it in its entirety, and cauterize the sore from its roots.  
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this one of an iron or steel chain according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not move it, to hold at the groin, and move pressing and if you see, so cauterize the tremble, as it is before in this chapter of cautery 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one ever makes a clyster of silver or lead, or molten iron or mesh; and never are these instruments made small and large according to those who they are administered to. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are given to administer in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small. 
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clyster is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner: 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a rupture where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is inside pierced; and on one side II pierced, and on the other I; and the belly where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole I must of space, then put in these holes I a strong thread of thread twisted in X or as much as around, and assemble the belly as it is a kid; and when the medicine is inside, tie the end in front of a strong thread, then give an enema; and this is the form of the circle:  
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And be the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the clyster with oil or with yolk of egg, or similar thing, then put it in gently; then the sprain the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all moist, then remove the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him strain as much as he can; and if he sleeps one whole night, then it is greater aid. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clench it for a malady of stomach ache, and the medicine comes out quickly, then he starts again until he is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or an abscess, then use the enema as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which the skin is restrained. 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to the fulfillment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to where the wounds are made, and from how they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of stone, and sword-cutting, and knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; which are done according to the places of the body, as a wound that falls upon the neck, or upon the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and will begin with the wounds of the head simple, for remembrance comes in its chapter.
