Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt a hot abscess: then make the patient bleed immediately from the cephalic vein even if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the injured part; and avoid the patient repletion of wine and fatty meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be lessened, and do not drink wine or eat meat. And put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in spiced wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not dried by the air, and powder that I will say a little later; and if it has been dried, put on some ointment until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by tents, then assemble them by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the stitch. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked barley, also lentils, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting wound and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rot, and throw away the pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, then you must cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light; and it is that you put in this powder which unites even as if fire had cauterized it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood II parts; quicklime III parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and restrain it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coal alone, when one has neither incense nor dragon's blood, but that the fire has cauterized the wound.  
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has cauterized the wound, even while still inflamed, do not put on this powder; but place some digested ointment or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it dries out; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, so extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you here after the fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.  
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to do but leave it alone and put nothing restricting, because it harms the nerve and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the medicine lukewarm, such as chalks washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and chalky wash also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist dressings.  
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so sew it together and tie with bandages, then treat until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bone is exposed and full of flesh, pierce or lower it; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes, then cauterize it, and bandage it; and if the windpipe of the throat is cut, or the veins, and the passage is kept, by which the meat goes, cut the heart above the base of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for several days, then cure it with ointment until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then set it; and if there are pieces of bone, then pull them out all that you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them as long as the wound suppurates, and be clean and aligned the opening; and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife  
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look at whether from the wound there are symptoms of wind as the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it tightly so that the blood does not stagnate, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that there comes no spasm, nor tremor of the heart nor strangeness of breath; and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is safe. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat then with tents and other dressings, as long as it is sound; and if it cannot heal and work, then know that there is a fistula; and treat the wound as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, so cure what is in front; if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is embedded in bone, and has chipped pieces, so cut the wound, and remove the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound rot, so that it will facilitate extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines come out, which causes introduction of some things; and the stitch is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound for that reason one puts the intestines back in, if one does not put them in hot in hot; because the intestine inflates as soon as they feel the cold, so they enter more into the point, and for this reason a medium wound becomes worse, for that reason one resets the intestine to its place than the others. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four ways: the two stitches common happen in the stitch of the belly, and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds; and nonetheless they are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will say one each and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the entrails has come out, and it is good to put things back in, this is done by one of the two ways: or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in boiling water only, or you cook in hot broth with squill and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this restraining, and be moved that it alone for deflation. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and bad herbs are cooked, because by this it is aligned the entrance a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that the tail, that no one should cut it except with great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: so trenched inside in the curve and outside no, and see here the form: 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has leapt out, set it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, for this is worth doing. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put what you have appeared, then hold in your hands the minister pitiful who holds all the rupture to his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound I a space of distance, and there pierce a needle where he has I good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the siphons, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierced on that side, and assemble the II heads of the siphon the IV together; then strain a double thread around the needle of II parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound equally, and then leave I space of distance, and there pierce another needle; then tie the end of the thread as you have done with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles, until the whole wound is bound; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, for the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they are medium; and it is not necessary to put the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient when he sleeps, and I put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles for them to hold tight, and let them remain until the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there suffices one needle or II the second stitch is common, and it is that you assemble the II heads of the skin and the II heads of the siphon together with a needle where he has I medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these heads all IV together, then pull back the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews cloth; and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger's breadth; this suture is useful for man, and I sewed a wound on one man’s belly, which was riddled with a knife, and it was a wound more than a palm wide, and there were intestines well II palms wide, and it was the wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed up to XV days, and I treated it, and he became healthy. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the men had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in that place where one found none, nor any medicines; and I put a cloth of old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it was healed.  
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the heart straight in straight, leave the tip of the needle where you have put it in or where you have sewn, and make it pierce on the other side from the inside out; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier does the furs, and that you leave once the point on one side and take it back on the other until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, that Galens says properly, is like any font, which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one end of the suture to the other end, in such a manner: stitch an needle or end of the suture close by, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside, through the two ends of the suture; then make it pierce both from the outside part to the inside, in two other sutures that are on the other side; and this is the best manner of suturing and the most common.  
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this saying, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with II needles, or there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more grievous than the others places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the arrow has moved it, then set back the intestine, and the outside; then put on powder enjaring flesh, and if the arrow has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and stitch the thread, and be soldered the skin, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to give bowe, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in many conditions as long as the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make commonality with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten linen lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in the bowels, which happens many times, then the clisterize with black wine, and even if the rot comes up to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is because of the placement of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon jumps from the wound, put it back as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or gray, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and put the two heads hanging from under the part of the wound until outside to align the extraction when the tendon falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw a man wounded in his belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and through it came excretion and flatulence; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to treat it until it was healed, and the edges joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient was poorly in his belly; and there was no evil, but he stayed in better dispositions, and ate and drank; and they said any experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such manner: take fremis to great heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the fremis had covered the mouth, she put it on the II lips, so that it strained its mouth up; and then he cut the head, and this stays so that it cannot untie, then put the other fremit after in the same manner as before, until the wound is all seized; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief if it is inflamed in the intestine, and there comes no nuisance to the patient, and one can tie the intestine of a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that be well cleaned, and then tie to the head of this thread I the thread of linen fine twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it in the rupture; and this manner of sewing of intestines is not forbidden except according to the way of fidelity and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be  
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is closed and goes inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knotted false boil and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in clear furrow, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is nothing but by one of the IX causes: that is to say, by the little bit of blood or flesh; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not let flesh be born; or there is too much furrow; or the lips are dry, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and late healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is therefore necessary for me to teach you the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so is it that comes to the property of the member principle, and the like members. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are this manner are of grief healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of iron or iron, if the fistula is straight, so the curve; and if the fistula is crooked, so the search with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends itself around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well search it by tents, so the cleanse it by one of the holes, because the moisture goes from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then search diligently with your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is cut off in its entirety, and ask well of the sick person the pain that he feels at pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, so act according to what I have told you, and remove the fault and the corrupt matter that are inside; and then treat until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep and straight, so it is necessary that you cut as deep as you can, then put moist tents in medicine strong, and push them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is lodged at the bottom; and then put ointment safe and sound flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these means, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it.  
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerves or principal members do not strike you, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure with things engendering flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns bowed as before, know that you are not well gone to the bottom: if uncover and seek until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it; if there is nothing else to leave to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it with pliers, if you extract it with the instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, so you pull them all, do not leave any one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, so cut and moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place on the wound something that prevents rot, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will more easily separate; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, let rest only the corruption as long as the blackness is completely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it comes to the marrow of the bone; then it must be soothed and covered until the corruption, and then cure it until it is fused; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the materials came to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the physicians by their folly opened so much that the abscess opened, and it oozed out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many holes that all dripped pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was running out through the holes a great deal; and the young man’s body became red, and had a yellowish color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that some came towards each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I put myself thus, and pricked in one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came to the inner bone; I was certain that what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not solder; and then again began, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to solder the place; but I could not more than I pricked around a palm of the bone, and the piece was all its mole, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and soldered quickly, and did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation of blood often, but he was healed entirely, and in the place of the bone grew hard cartilage, and was of good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary from all things, neither to go nor to come. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it must be treated this way: take a linen cloth, and strain it at the head of the bone which opens, and command anyone that he extend it upwards; and put another linen bandage thicker than the first bandage, and tie it over the flesh which is above the bone, and stand the head so that you pull the corrupt flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh on the place where you want to be, that the sinew does not bleach the flesh; and put a charcoal or a plank under the bone for to cover the corrupt flesh; and must be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and be treated again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh completely; then put the burning stick below, and then move it from one side to the other of the corruption, and let the suture be as long as the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupt joint, and suture the bone where it contains from the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to do but to cut; and if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand or in the thumb of the foot, this thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve does not oppose you; and know that the incisor and the probes to cover these bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their subtleness, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so think about the instrument which you need according to what is proper.  
dou feu	of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be affected by causes from within or from outside; and when you have treated the corruption with medicines and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from so that the patient escapes either by this means from death, or by the evil, which is greater, of the defect of the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, then comes the corruption from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; so hurry in covering it, and if it is because of the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar ones, if the corruption is at the head of the arm, cover it, and do not give it any space to come up to the hand.  
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no further treatment worth than the quantity of its virtue; and do thus when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes at the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, cut all the foot; and if it mounts up to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way but to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or treating the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister from one ligature downwards, and another minister the other ligament upwards, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ligaments at a spatula wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or treat it, and put on each side the drape of linen, so that the treatment does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the place well, or put some powders restraining on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in his foot: he had a black spot which seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came into his toes of the foot, until it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and it was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned to him in the palm of the hand, and he came to me, and I put things on him that were effective after the purification of the body, and could not cease the corrosions; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of restoring the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have told this tale only for this reason: so that you can do it differently, if you need. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes to a head, and stays for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and leaks, and the pus jumps out, like vessels; and the skin above is as thin as fine linen, and does not go down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such disease is called "boil", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is so thin that you can cut through the skin all around, even when it is as thin as linen; and it does not close up for its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have the belief that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not completely there, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema like this: look if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it has a foul odor, then enema with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take asafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them into a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and enema the breast, and restrain the anus; and leave the medicine inside for II hours, then withdraw it by pressing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the stench is removed; and sometimes enema with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, and that you take the ashes of vinewood, and pour water on top, then filter it, and enema, until you know that the breast is well cleaned; and if the sick person cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then enema with water and honey where there is a pinch of powdered litharge; or enema with honey and sweet wine, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine dries out the flesh; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then enema with something which makes flesh grow in it, and that is to take diaphana plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine; or enema with other medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken their properties or treatment of ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter, then widen a piece of iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then stitch and leave only the space where the enema can enter, and if the opening that gives off stench is above, then plug it lower down than its position.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the breast is set right, do not let anything be put on it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare in such a way that the breast goes to the lowest point that it is, because when the breast is well set, do not let anything be put on it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare in such a way: that the breast goes down gently, and let nothing of the breast remain; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place on top of the linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then cut as hard as possible at the bottom of the breast a little wider than the first, then place ointment underneath the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and place it on the wound of the breast to align the breast, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and he who is on the bottom of the breast, often removed to remove the breast, and know what comes from the breast, whether it is poison or blood or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or no pain, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is spread in such a way and you see the nature that jumps on the wound of the breast, then know that the breasts are already hardening, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed improperly after many days, know that the breast does not heal well. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and some who do the opposite; and if a boil that indigested from the breast after many days, know that the breasts do not heal well; and if the breasts are late to heal, and are far apart, then apply medicines drying moist in substance and dry in virtue, like diaphinit ointment, for there is much vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine. Take diaphinit ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and the essence of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same made honey cooked, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take frankincense and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire; and then glue it to the breast, and put it on the breast, and at any time administer a long arilloge, and roots of celestial lilies, which are also like flour of quince and centaury; and use simple or compound: grind them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is lengthy, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is deep, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in members; like the cure of a fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or by chance it arises in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, there comes I the abscess worsens, and runs and gets worse until it corrodes the root of the nail, and perhaps it corrupts the whole; and the corrosion comes up to the bone, so that there comes pungent pain, and the limb of the leg is wide, and the color is inflamed.   
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must cut away all the superfluity that is remaining from the wound, then cauterize the wound afterward. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail follows the flesh inside, and it begins to prick and bleed, then you must put a light under the nail so that it does not reach the flesh, and put it upwards, and cut that flesh finely and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines hot and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat it, because as much as the bone is corrupted there, so it cannot heal; and if you see that it should be corroded, then cut it in I like it was said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken and pushed, and he feels great pain, then you must heal him first; then cut the angle of the spatula with a sharp edge cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder of the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in any of us of the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any knot of the thigh does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the thigh, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy so it is light, in such manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so it holds you to cut.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be at the last our, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable line for it, then cure it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The seizures that come to the two joints come by birth, or by wound welding, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.  
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you bind that joint, so that the parts return according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of fine wood, as long as the bones are united, as it is necessary.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a seizure comes upon one of his two hands with the palm, so seize that seizure as it befits.  
des vils	of evils 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large swollen vessels full of melancholy superfluities, which come in more than members of the body; and more often happen in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than to others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary for you to administer once purge of oil, and then heal with the basilica.  
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut and drain the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it completely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The thigh is done in this manner: first raise the leg of hot water very strongly, until the hard flesh is softened; then strain the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; then cut open the vein in I place, or II or III, with a wide incision; then let the blood flow and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the patient can endure; and then band it up, and command him that he lie down on meats cooked over charcoal black; and restart the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner: place the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, and then cut the vein long from the top of the knee to the bottom of the foot, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a knife, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it; and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the point underneath, until it is elevated from the skin, and then bind it to the knife lightly, then cut in another place above III times; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the base, as you have done, and bind it to another knife, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the bottom of the foot, then pull and lift until the second section; then extract from section to section, until it is all pushed out, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle in the whole strong double thread, and tie it and pull it, and put it underneath the point, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and keep it from cutting, because if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have treated it completely, put on the wound a piece of wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and enclosed altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twistedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut deeply, so that it only cuts the vein; and is thick in curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein deeper, but let it be as thick as we have said, and here is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where no herbs nor trees are born, and in earth where it has no moisture; and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the rotting that comes from under the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, nestled between skin and flesh.  
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its color, and the vein begins to swell out as much as the root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
