When the head is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to II III., and tie it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and all times that it is painful in front of the fire, then wrap around the cloth, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remaining, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out; because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings about an abscess and rot there, and bad illness; for that reason, it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remain in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated is of V palms of long, or X, and one time a man came to me, whose it was of X palms long, and when you cut it, it puts out the root with its end, and pierces it to the bottom so that everything comes out; and be emptied the matter that is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing rot any day, then cure it as the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein it comes to a standstill, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or leg, and there comes much blood loss, and from which it comes out by itself; treat it therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land “ox disease,” because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the end of limb by limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and jumps; and it is generated from putrefaction of some humors, like worms and serpents and embers and ascarids in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him cured and treated, it is not possible to move him except when he goes: so it behooves you to tie the place above and below with a strong linen very tightly, then cut above and treat the wound, and if the thread is pulled into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see him coming or chief near the eye, then strain under him the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and treat the wound; and it behooves the patient to use purification of body medicines solutives for humors diseases, and avoid meats causing corruption. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This sickness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then a little after corrupted throughout the whole body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she returned as if around the body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.  
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I wanted many to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want that, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed, and for this reason appeared that constrained windiness; and they did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then lie above and below gently, and then cut up until the wind-filled (cavity) is constrained in its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with what dispels wind-filled (cavities), such as fetid pills, and pills of serpent's root, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large points, and small, and haired, and welded; and those which have II angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces; and those which fall in any limb so it falls in II manners: or in the principal member it falls, such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you after, appear to you: then it befits that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not entirely embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the syfache which is on the brain, is when it is scotome and sudden and overturned and bloody in the eyes, and inflammation and blood of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without breath from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and leaps from the wound white moisture seeming to poultices, and leaps also like burning of flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold from treatment, and treat the arrow if it is not inside.   
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seven when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left side of the mother, and feels as if it were tied in a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the seven moves also like the hand, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and sweat cold, and fainting: know then without doubt that death comes.   
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces low is that without plains of foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.  
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and causes great pain and great suffering and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulder.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound any thing of undigested meat. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and there is no point of sinew by the intestine rout, then there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.  
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out in leaps and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and thighs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to more dispositions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do something else. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that shot into the root of the nose: I grasped it and pulled it out from another side beneath the ear fat, and it was healed without feeling at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a game, an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye under the paper under, and the arrow was put back, and I could only reach it with the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, to all the iron light without ears; the game was safe, and no bad accidents came to him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I pulled the barbs out, and carefully until I drew it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow in a man, that was lodged in his side or belly, and thought he would die; and then after he had passed XXX days, it did not change its position; I cut upon the arrow, and tightened it, and treated it, and there was no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow in his buttock or back, and the wound is stitched up; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor does he feel any discomfort in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and remained so suffering great pain; and many other similar things.  
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow to the prince's man, who it was in his middle, and was a little declining on the right side; and the arrow was whole, I was called for treatment after it fell three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.  
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt her with a whole subtle tent, and I felt it not at all; and she felt prickling and pain below her right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the poultice on for several days, and sutured the wound directly, and kept the patient that way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his thigh; and he told me.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put upon the wound medicine sharp corrosive for several days, until it was open, and I felt, and sensed the head of the arrow which hardened in place; then I adjusted in the opening of the wound by that medicine sharp, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it pierced well the ends for four months, and then widened so much the wound that I put in the pliers, and my hand on one side and the other, and it could not issue; therefore I did not cease to subtilize and to devise instruments in many ways, until I took one day the pliers well made, according to those which its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I treated it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the mirror judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those that I do not say, because the books cannot take everything; but the wise masters look at a very small thing, and on those that are present and failing, find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not found in the limbs where they are lodged except according to two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is found by the place where it enters, is an arrow entering its flesh, and that which is none of these times. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it be left until the flesh is carried around, and let the issue be healed; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot move, let it be left so for several days, and let it be moved each day; and then if it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around it with a fine needle, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not extract it, but leave it as long as it is equal after a few days, because if the arrow comes to such a place, it is death.  
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone only, and does not come to its tip, and the patient stays for some days without bad accident, then the machine of the milking. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very tight thus and cannot come loose further, then administer compresses around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and if one cannot see it, if he wishes to search for it all around; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the depth of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then cut as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrow to which it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck on both sides until you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, so that you would extract it more painfully. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until the surrounding tissue is softened, then treat it, for extraction is easier.  
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding does you harm, so administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter; and guard yourself from cutting the nerve and the vein, and put engine as much as you can move to draw the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, so put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where nothing is opened of it, or the skin is swollen in that place so that one sees or feels it clearly: cut then above, as long as the tongs can take it, and then extract it: if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then drive it. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if it is of the shaft, put it to the whole shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see administer pushing, then administer the instrument headfirst, so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push, and if the arrow is headed, then put the instrument in pointed entry, to facilitate extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it is fitting. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs and it is near, and you can cover it up, if you cover it; and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if need be; and cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an owl, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the blunt point is like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as here it is the form. 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for inserting and holding is as follows: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of veins from which one heals are XXXI, of which there is at the head XVI, that is to say: II veins which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in the II temples apparent; and II veins which are in II tear ducts of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the two; and the II veins which are on the neck; and the II veins which are in lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augeherich"; and II veins which are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins by which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: one is the cephalic and is on the left side of the rib cage, and the common people call it “vein of the head”; and the middle one is called "faste" and is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side of the rib cage, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fossa, and it is the one by which one bleeds, which opens manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two of them; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the curve of the pocket of the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse," which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins under those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old coughs and migraines; and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tightly strangle the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependent places on the head: where those then to your side, and where you feel the pulse under your hip, sign there; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the whole vein above, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two times of traversing, and make blood flow as much as you see; then strain and tie, until it is cured; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is worth for headache ancient, and sudden, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of the tears sharp eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding si is as I say: and is that the patient restrains his neck, so long as the two veins appear openly; and feels the pulse below your right, and then reign in; then lift the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet below, and lift the vein up, and the cup, as you have done in the other two veins, and make correct of the blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right on the vein an hour, then put on cotton; and then the lie form, and leave it as long as it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cutting and their extraction, where begins the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the front head is as valuable as the cephalic vein for old facial ailments, and for migraine and redness; and the qualities are that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digger", whose form is:  
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and steady with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then tie up the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and never work it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right that the flames are too large; and the skin should be cut across, because the bone is near, and by chance it breaks the flames when it is thin. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the ear, and the cheek, and to the root of the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a rope as before; then the vein, and let the vein be through, a piece through long of flame a piece wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie on cloth, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the arm near the nose is good for fever, and for sore throat, and for ailments of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his collar, then strains his nostril with your left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and sticks it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in this way, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep into it, and make it correct according to your need, then tie it at night, because it is restored very quickly; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II veins helps in the treatment of the ailment, and at the beginning of meselerie, and many diseases, and epilepsy, and corrosions, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient strains his neck beneath one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on top of the head of the patient, and the patient lying on the seat, then open the vein with a long incision, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as needed; then re-do another part in the other vein, then untie the linen, and strain both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until the morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and wounds of the gums and tongue.  
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: cut therefore both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and just as well do the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and for illnesses of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein: so bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep into it, for below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins to be cut which are commonly opened are opened in two ways: either pricked at the whole flame with a sharp, thin point, like trenchant cutters, and are called «aneils»; and they are wide and fine according to the width and depth of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is very well known, and is wide as you see. 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are flat and full of large visible blood, and which contain large and troubled blood; and this is the form of olive flame.  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the veins subtly, where there is subtly yellow blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it behooves the physician to draw blood wisely, and that he keep himself away from the artery which is under. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the earth, and running of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; and it must not be piercing the flame, but cutting like an anvil. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it behooves you to restrain it, and change another; or you desire no vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein removed from the arm; it opens manifestly; and the cup at the flame anesil, as we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you extract the arm so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse; then sign the place with a cautery, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame without fail; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: therefore shun it.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the vein is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and put your hand above lengthways, then remove your hand if the vein is still there; this happens many times; bind his arm, and leave him so, and do not move him the patient; and be in fear, and do not move him until he is sound. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the vein is not cleansed and it bothers you, and no medicine is present, so close the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and cleanse the vein. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of fig, and make it split, and take one half and bind it well until the other day; if it does not sting, that is good; if it does not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping is not harmful in more dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligament.   
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the patient to lean on the nerve which is below, and if he is not too much affected, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates and the saints are griped, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men for its subtlety, then you must use the instrument to drain; and feel the nerve with your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make it long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head helps so that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest position, and it does not harm if it must be done the first time, and one begins again; and by chance it swells the joints in some men, when one does it the first time, but it does not harm. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of blood is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, is that bloodletting is administered only to preserve health and to avoid diseases to come; and the bloodletting is done in one of the three veins which are or called: namely cephalic, brachial, and basilica; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring on foot, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered to diseases has no set time, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not proper to bleed children until XIV years, nor a woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Those over sixty years old should not bleed. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some wants to bleed, in whatever manner that it may be, it is necessary that he purge the intestines with a light enema, if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines superfluities corrupted and harmful to the principal members; nor should anyone bleed who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk, as long as he is in that state, nor those who are dropsy; and worse it is to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea of the belly, and multiplication of childbirth, and labor, and watching, and fasting, and all things that diminish or increase the virtues of either arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if his blood is thick, by meat and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so; then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be silent and joyful, and let the bleeder stand higher than him who bleeds, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the bandage above in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with his hands, until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the bleeder's flame with a bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein below the wrist where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail when it is punctured.  
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords in the healthy, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and so is one of these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too tight, for which reason it is necessary that the physicians be warned about these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, it must be started again a little below where it was tried, if the place is not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: by chance there will come boils; nor enter into hot water, since he starts bleeding again if he likes; and if the wound is small, or the vein is subtle and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, then trust in that same wound all the flame straightly; and make a hole gently, so that the limb is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.  
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin the bleeding again, and put on a bit of oil ointment, for it closes the body's blood, and is mixed in this place the oil that; and so administer the ointment of oil in every wound that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing works triacle and balm of them, when one puts it on the place; so subtle is the sap and spreads when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there come an abscess big, which happens often, even when it is not drained except at the time when the opening of the vein is small, hasten yourself, and put upon the place a sponge moistened in water and a little hot, and restrain it for one hour; and it behoves that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days without any blackness or greening, it harms him not; and if you see, put upon it nothing of aloes or myrrh put in juice of calamine, monstastre, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and swelling appear on the flesh of the basilica: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then is that swelling bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place on that any of what we have said, because by chance it might pierce the artery; but make it a dry plaster to harden the place, then cure it with other cures, until it is healed.  
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it stay until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is plump and full, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed him little by little and often, and he must be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from decorrement of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is worth more than the bleeding by long or wide.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give soft bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, treat him with blood III times or IV. And if he is of cold complexion, warm before bleeding soft bread in quince syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pulses at the vein, after the outflow of much blood, it is necessary that he moisten broth of flesh, and fragrant syrup, subtle, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty his arm, and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he bleeds a little and a little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to drain his arm after the first vein opening, and he has strong flesh, then heals VII hours after the first vein opening, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another side, they must bleed the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body that has already been consumed, and brings fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening as much as he will bleed in pieces; then when you have rewarded all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come into the place of pieces, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it does not become necessary when you see to release the arm, and make blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press heavily upon it; nor if it is curved, that you extend the arm fully, for this would be bad; but let him rest until he heals a second time; or you put a point to the flame, as long as the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out, and put on top a piece of wool placed in water, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to bleed a second time, then in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein of the arm is bled at the place of the vein of the head because it is composed there. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then be it tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then the incision now through, neither wide nor long; and let the openings be wide, and let it be incised well near the joint of the hand, and if he cannot extract it, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood to run until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the incision of this vein is safer of all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salve of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one sees it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it through completely, it does not harm anything; and do not go too deep in cutting it, because the nerves are under all exposed flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you will have treated of the blood as much as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and wool to soothe it well, and thus do for each vein.  
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of it in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you for the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the knees, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and legs ancients, and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his healing is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it throbs, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; heal therefore either the wider vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, guard the nerves which are below, and heal in passing as when cutting; and let the flames be anemic. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be drawn out, then put your foot into the water, and let the vein flow well.  
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient feels pain the first time, begin again above a little bit, because the wound is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the same incision on the other foot evenly. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic is at the ankle of fury, and its pain reaches to the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood.  
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein are that the patient enters into water bath and pulls up over the ankle four fingers by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you close it in all ways that you can, and crossing; and it is better that you cut it, because the wound is dry, and she is much swollen with hands of men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy any rain of him who opens or back of the foot, and towards the small thigh, and guard the nerves; and make so much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the tie, and put on cotton and constrain; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups  
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suckers are made of horns, or lead, or glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is meant to hurt so is according to two manners: or it is with fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by pricking and extracting blood is done in XIV places of the body, for one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the cup on below the chin; and the cup on the II shoulders; and the cup on the hips; and the cups in the II arms; and the cups in the II legs; and the cups in the II ankles; and cupping does not deal with blood, except for small veins that are spread in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken one as much, as one does from bloodletting of a vein; and it should not be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any disease which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to bleed, or for customs, we bring them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are such that, when they have need to bleed, they have a heavy head; and so there are who feel repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and spit blood; and there are such who dream, and see by blood and fogs and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed from the month, we command to ventilate after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the vein helps in the great pain of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it does not behoove that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it does not behoove those who are of a cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because it causes them great discomfort; and for this reason it does not behoove the elderly to use it, nor those who have or head colds diseases. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it, often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down because of the fear of obliviousness. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windpipe in the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of a bad cough, and for cutting the channel of the throat, and for all things, and for filling; and it should not be squeezed too tightly, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause blockage in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The fumigations at the II ribs of the neck are good for pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the patient to spread his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not come hemorrhages of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The mouth ventilation under the chin is good for mouth disease and gum rot, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the health of the lower lips.  
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness coming from heat and fullness. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The incisions of the veins are as good as III veins in the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to make them too deep, because the skin is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.   
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is on the rump is good against hemorrhoids of the foundation, and against diseases below, and it behoves that the leech be large, and be of iron, so that it has need to well draw; and perchance, if it were subtle, it would break; and thus makes great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping on the legs is very effective because they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains in the kidneys, the stomach, and the bladder, and reduce swelling; and they are placed on the two shins, and the two ankles, but nevertheless, they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness to many positions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the cupping glass is that you put it first empty, and then moderately, and place it gently, and move it equally, and do not cease to do so until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then fire, and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have tight flesh, and clear pores: therefore it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a deep prick; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it behooves to strike it twice; the first time to open up the path of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we suck only once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, so often we return; and if the vein is thick, then apply a fire ember to it, and that end that the veins be pierced soundly, and it behooves him who has thick and hard skin, and who has strong pores, that you oil the places of the ventosa with an aromatic and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed; and if it is in winter, of cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of wormwood, or of balsam, or oil of rue, and similar.
