Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is being healed has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, if he rises from it, or from myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities get up from old wine, or water of seuc, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar; and it does not become good to bleed with a ventouse before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or II; and do not sleep after the ventosation, and it becomes that he gets up, when he should be venteoused and when he is venteoused. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And ward that one who is healing is choleric, and if his flesh is too hot and inflamed; then it behoves him to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the meal, and similar things; and milk porridges, and roasted meat, and moist meats.  
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and millet flour, and millet cake, and small birds, sparrows, and pigeons; and on the day he will be bled, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men once triacle or musk before the bleeding, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let the taste be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot should drink it.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without hurting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips and the pelvis, because these members do not suffer being injured on their own, and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb, like we put them on the nipples when the baby is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, like we put suction cups on the belly and on the groin to lessen the member; and remove the pain, when there is an abscess or stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the abscess, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts them on the liver and on the spleen when there is wind retention, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and some times filled with warm water, like in illnesses of the pleursin, and in such a manner one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water where herbs have been boiled suitable for that. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it shall have two boards of breadth and half a palm from front to back, and it shall have on the side or in the middle a small hole, as for putting a needle, and be of iron, soft beforehand so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb; and in the middle it shall have a bar across of iron or steel, to put a candle held tight, and let them be large and small according to the ailments and the age of those who take them; for the cupping glasses of children are other than old people's, and of thin people than fat.   
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus place this suction cup upon the limb: take hold of the candle of wax or the lining, and place it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the clarity be at the bottom of the suction cup that it not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the openings should be on the opening that we have said, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes in, and one removes the suction cup; and take hold of the lining as before, and re-do it often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, to any acute pain, has no rod or aperture, and is not administered except when it is full of liquid, and is placed on the member only so much; and this is the form. 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech are brought only to members where one cannot put leeches because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar; and in the exposed flesh, such as two or three, and others similar; and the qualities of using it is that when you find leeches that are in clear sweet water without any dirt, take them; and put them in a nut of sweet water until they are full, and have nothing in their bellies; and then drain them of blood and leech, then rub the member until it is red, and put the leeches on top; and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a leech, put it on, because it is very good afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, then raise the place of ease, and then water, very well, and then strain it; and if the wounds heal too quickly after the body of the sinuses, then moisten the cloth of linen in cold water, and put on top, until the sinus is extended; and if the sinuses are multiplied, then put on top powdered vitriol, or salt, and similar things, until it is extended; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them as long as they dry on the place, so it will now stop; and if you need more, then take other sinuses.  
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sutures do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you put a needle there until the sutures come out, and then put them back on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick; and when you see that they are sticking, put some powder of aloes and willow bark ground up, or ashes on top, and now they will hold.  
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the fool who looks in this chapter, will never see anything from ancient books, nor read any letter; and for this reason is hidden knowledge in our land, because I have never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have taught you in this chapter what is contained, and have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments which are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It therefore behooves us to say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the sages place their understanding, and remain on the truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if no thing does not him well, such as weakness of body, or child, or old man; or if his temper is not very hot, or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say, cold dishes, and flesh of deer and lamb, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with meats which fill the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt of a hot abscess, nor expansion of matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to his first government that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or which have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and feet, and entrails of veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such twisting they are renewed and more quickly healed fractures. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken of old and decrepit people cannot well be rejoined or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, like the bones of small children; but make no cure, set on the broken bone the thick tendons that hurt and join the limb together, as much as it forces as it was before; and not in any part of its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish them with thick meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, or of the arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to a point, and others when sharpening, like the nib of a pen for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture to a whole small fissure. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its engine, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which the ends are twisted, and open well by outside, and feels at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor feel on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no fracture; but it can well have torsion, or rupture, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit that you move it by hand, but put upon medicines which come after here, and then restrain it subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in a curve, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them together equally, so that abscesses do not come; and if abscesses do come, let him leave none day, until the abscesses are quieted; then put it together like you can lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of the one that has pieces; then restrain it, as it is necessary after. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in two parts, if it's the hands or feet, or to the hand if it's a small limb, or to two ropes, or to one rope and to the hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are freed, you set by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work comes no lesion nor pain to the patient; and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: so straighten it beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, carefully instruct the patient that they do not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the limb be so assured that he feel no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it is necessary to put him in such a disposition that he feels no pain; and guard yourself that he be placed straight, that tortuosities do not come when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape.  
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: so it is necessary to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: so it is necessary to envelop them with a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no void; then bind around light poultices, three turns or four according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, than the fracture pushes a little away from the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you feel the healthy part of it, then take the other bandage, and turn around straight over the broken place; then return to the part below the fracture, and tighten moderately, not too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; then put between the bandages poultices of linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on it a soothing thing for the abscess, hot, and which removes the swelling, and let it so for some days; then restrain with bands of its stars, and be half an inch wide carefully, or of wood from which they make staffs, or of palm branches, and be according to this figure:  
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is appropriate to the member of smallness or largeness; then bind over the splints as you have done at the first hour, then tie above with a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; more tight on top, less below; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want from works of the fools who do their bindings with cords of twisted linen, and this is great error, because the binding cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit at all that there be between each splint less than two fingers' width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the bones of the shoulders after the strapping in their healthy parts, then put under them compresses of linen or wool felt so that it does not become inflamed. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bones are broken, I will say its cure here after.  
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to tightly bind all broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it does not come convenient to put splints for after V days or VII, or more according to your certainty of an abscess occurring; and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour that keeps on the walls of the mill, and confect it with plenty of egg, and put this confection, neither too light nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of plaster restoring the fracture in many dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  abaeris and ladani and enule and asafetide and gum arabic and mugat, ana X III.; mirr and aloes, ana V III.; alechil VIIII III.; and make it into powder, and mix it with yolk of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is good for many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of poultice that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana X Z; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII Z; acacia VI Z; Armenian bole X Z, and grind well, and confit with water or white of egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones dislocated from their places, and appease the pain arising, and the size used of the bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in honey and oil cooked, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [the body], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly takes away the pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and earth laurel leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of emplaster for the restoration of the broken bone and to lessen the remaining of the abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of quince, one part each; and grind, and confection with wine, and if the limb is numb, confect it with moist coriander water, or water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to set a bone more firmly than the first, when an abscess prevents the restoration of the limb.  
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marshmallow, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and comfrey, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and confit with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its repose. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should put on the broken limb a restorative made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and the heads of men's hair, or feathers of birds, and wormwood, and flax, all equally, and grind them up, and make it into a plaster and apply it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you undo it a little later, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if the bones have moved from their place; if they do not undo it for many days And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and undo it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light bandage, and a sponge of wet sea, and dip in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a nut, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin the fine bandage again, and a little plaster, and do not restrain it as strongly as before; and continue finely until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has pus and redness and pain and swelling are all there, and you need to apply poultice and linen, if it begins again, just as you did at the first doing. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb of those that we have said, so do not loosen it before III days or IV or V or VII; and no time leaves it XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals, and approaches the fitting of the bone above; therefore restrain it more than first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see it drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; rose then of hot water tide, all times when you loosen it, and this be each third day, and ease a little the lieure; by this work therefore shortens the nourishment to the limb, and amends hastily those that do the foolish mire, that remained the limb tortured: this is evil, and so is dangerous works, and I see no other thing than to leave it and work it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various manners of fracture 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the shaft which is below the bone, as made high or low; and because of this, this manner of fracture is called “haichure”. 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is great or small.  
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impacted percussion, or fissure or of neck of stone, or of heel upon stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture piercing, which approaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is put back in the bone as subtle as a horse hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by striking with stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and it puts the piece of bone inward, and the ends are shaped like those of the blacksmith when he heats them on the cauldron; so between the bones inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or whose head is moist bones, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are broken off from them like splinters; and I will speak of it in its place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by pulling on them, and the questioning with probes, and by the rotten flesh that is above. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair capillary is known by this that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed above it, the black fracture opens. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of accidents in the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, and emission of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever with chills, and eyes red and bulging, and other similar things in more dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unavoidable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone does not rot, and the accident we have mentioned comes about.  
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you cut the split part thus: and it is that you prick the head of the patient carefully, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more gently than you can, and if a discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, apply a poultice, help as needed, and fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the poultice is appeased, and be assured of no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut at the narrowest edge before, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts another piece larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and of iron; and in work lightly, that you do not bruise the chief. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is stiff and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it through, so that you administer splints with awls, lest they go through the bone beyond, and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that each comes in its place of the width of the bone, so that you have awls for all bones; and this is the form of the three kinds of splints: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to perceive around the broken bone is that you put the probe on the bone, and turn at your sides until you know that the bone is perceived; then put the probe elsewhere a little after, and so do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and make those more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers; and keep that you do not touch the brain nor the syfac. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have the bone perceived and treated, it is necessary that you reset the apparatus which is stayed from the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tenves and more subtilz than the other incisor; and if there remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then cure the wound lightly with the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galien says, which is drier; and he praised it a lot, and this is his word.  
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put beneath the head of this lenticular incision, for this is the form: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the part is acute in II coasts, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and give yourself good guard of the cloth that is beneath; if it is adhered to the bone, gently remove it, because one removes it well without annoyance, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach to the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to rere that asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the figure of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If one shaves before with a large razor, and after with more subtle ones, and does not cease doing so until it is well. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other cuts of hair and subtle fracture, it is necessary that you bring cause according to its arrangement; and this thing is not replied to him who has put his study in this art.  
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the suppurating wound is open, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not burden the suppurating wound, then administer from above another linen bandage, and do not tighten it more than so much as it alone holds the wound; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the pus has calmed; then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of vetiver, and incense powder, and arnica, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer other medicinal unguents without stinging; and watch that the wound be always clean, that you leave no oil in it, nor let any pus gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's cloth, it will corrode and fester, and bring great harm to the patient; for when one puts a stinging thing on the suppurating wound, it will sting from above. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if no evil accidents come to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.  
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no blackening comes out except for the medicine that has been put on it, which has virtue, then it is necessary that you mix a part of honey and III parts of rose oil and glue one drapel, and put it on the wound; then cure it in ways of cures as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the bone above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it behooves you to put your small finger or pierce through the two, and place each fracture inside your index finger, and with your thumb on the outside, until the bones return according to their natural shape; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain by your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the cheekbone and it cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it even with the head of a stick a little thick.  
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, then make another splint, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or the tenth, when the abscess has calmed down, then bind with a cloth band around the head, in one part.  
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one on top of the other, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the wounds. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said any restorative one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the preparation of auburn from an egg and powdered millet; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in place of tents, and if the wind blows around it, it holds the wound, and blows on the patient; do as you see fit. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you work on it, put a cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in the pock of diaquillon. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put a plaster from outside of sesame flour and frankincense powder, confited with egg yolk, then put light tampons on top, and do not tie it at all; and if the fracture of the bones is small and broken into small pieces, so extract them with suitable instruments, then sew the fissure, and the cure of things in order to flesh, and soldering, as suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the bone, so cure it with tents, and put wads of wool, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated down, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outside, and is not broken in two, except that it is splintered inside, if one knows it lightly.  
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It behooves, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture gently inside, and make it firm with the other hand outside, and set it straight. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced into two, it is necessary that you administer extension to both parts, until they are equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a fracture, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw a cerote, and put on top a double cloth; and put on the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then undo it on the third day, and then put back in place what is changed; and put a plaster above, of powder from the mill with abundance of egg or sesame flour, after that you have removed the cerote; and put above the plaster linen light, and if the plasters harden, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave him as long as he is sound; many times it is sound in III weeks.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward that no piece of the bone is removed; so subtle to remove with instruments suitable to this.  
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on its top bandages suitable to those, so that it may hinder flesh, until it be healed. 
de la forcele	of the forceps 
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks more often in front, toward the shoulder, and the fracture is according to III manners: or it is broken and separated in II, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without wound, that you have II ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the force of the fracture; and the other stretches the neck toward the side; then put equal the fracture to your two hands, so that the form be as it should, and there is no appearance or defect.  
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be it large according to your necessity; and being and light the forcele, and restrain the sphere in your hand, so that you put equal the break, as it conviene. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the bone out by force because it comes embedded, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back and put below the shoulder the lower edge of the arm, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.  
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your two hands, and if you find it broken in pieces, it is necessary that you cut above; and gently separate the pieces, and if the bones cannot join by any elevation, then sever one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the forceps this instrument, to guard against the syfac.  
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not wholly hollowed out, and be as wide as it is required, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have II heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then dress the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come there, moisten the cloth in rose oil and asel and wine, and put it on. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is sensed in wounds and in incisions, is that you put upon the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of the yolk of egg, and put light bandages above, and put a spear under the armpit, if you have need; then take a very large bandage of a palm wide, then put the double drape above bandages, and the plaster; then take an estele subtle of III spans wide and long, and envelop it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the estele above the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and tighten it from each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the estele does not move above the broken bone, then you reward it every day, and when the bandages loosen, then you restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small pillow under the armpit, to raise the shoulder upwards; so will ease the fracture of the force by the lifting of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it unless bad accident comes, until XX days; then renew the plaster, if you see that he has need, and restrain and leave it as such, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most XXVIII days, and in less time for some people. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	There are times that the shoulder breaks or splits in the middle, and it is not known until by touch; then arrange according to the figure of the fracture, and set it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put on the location powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on top a double cloth. Then put on top a broad and fine splint, a little more broad than the shoulder, and if the splint rests upon any part of the shoulder, so use those hairs as splints of linen, so that the splint sits equally; and then hold it with a very firm bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the connection every day; and every time that it softens, tighten, and put back into place the splint if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, because it is not a bone which sets easily.  
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is exposed before and not under the heart, do it like this, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe an abscess hot. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg 
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the midst, it falls downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and cough, and perhaps vomiting blood, and opens the channels in the broken bone, and it feels warm to the touch.  
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies flat on his back, and you put a cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and subtly try to align everything in every way that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put bandages and padding above the thin layer of salt, or other light paste, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and restrict it constantly, and re-wrap every hour the bandaging, and if it softens, bind it again; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and clean what has come from cures; then reapply the bandage, and restrict it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only in their thickness after the back, and at the head within, and they bend only for this reason because they are glazed; and one feels it well to the inquiry on both sides. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture even, as it behoves. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on the splint, and restrain it with a strap if you need it. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, the patient feels great pain and throbbing, as well as pleuresin, because the bone pierces the skin; and also to stitches, and coughs and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients put great effort into it. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to drive the wind outward.  
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, except that boils come when they haven't.  
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes to him, heal it. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that some put cupping glasses on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw the superfluities to the place for the arrangement of weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said of each one that one should cover the place with wool moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the heat around it, then be cured from the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain which he cannot bear from the bone which pierces the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it behooves to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it behoves to put underneath an instrument to guard the sifac; and therefore one must trench the bone, and draw gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on soft cloths in rose oil, and put them on top; and cure while the place of it is fit for the abscess, and be lying sideways on the side where it should be, as long as it is healed.   
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that they bend; and also in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, if you take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing.  
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when being pulled and straightened, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care into it. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take care if the legs are soft, and if the accident is in their hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without will; and when one has laid it on its belly, then there is excretion without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is placed on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if one does not work in its care.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is the lighter thing. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, then put on the spine olive rose or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are broken, it is necessary to cover over the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment to incite flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', put your pouch in your left hand, and set it equal to the other hand at your power, then place the splint and the splint on top, if you need them; then restrain it, and if there are bones dislocated, do so above, and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there has not been much weakening at the head; and made long, and declining to the side, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and tingling, and inflates that which breaks. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the figure of it; and if the fracture is in the head only, then put equal the fracture, as long as it is to a natural figure. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it bends inwards, then make the patient lie on their belly, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it equal, put it on the plaster, then put on a stick or kernel on top, and restrain the bandage so that it does not move; and apply the place below the ribs until the limb is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
