Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and hold it as it should, if there are no bad accidents; and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The helpers is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a stick straight of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with bands, and raise them up, and set the patient on the stool; then place his broken arm on the stick, as far as it comes to the armpit, and have a bend in the stick, then put on any heavy thing or the ministers extend it down; then put the splints equal in his hands together, until the splint returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his head, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands the two ministers that one holds those who are above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds below all the limb, and extends each to its part. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, restrain the limb below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to its side. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one linen band under the armpit, and the other towards the outside, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the outside, then it is necessary to put the linen band lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on top and on the side; then set the fracture as it should, and restrain it, if a suppurating boil does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes to it, do not restrain it until VII days, and put on a linen cloth half in oil and rose oil, until the abscess is appeased; then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you put the plaster on the wound, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the cloth, and restrain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm be in its place as much as anything does not prevent it, or if the bone is not moved.  
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint 1 part of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture 3 parts on each side; then press upwards on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more forcefully and less in a widening.  
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess hot, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or that inflammation may not come to the limb because it is too much strained. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.  
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents happens, then do not unbind it for more than III days or so, and have the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and watch every hour of the day or of the night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments do not soften; if it is set by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat which we have before said, in such a manner that the meat be at first thin; and when it begins to recover, then let it be thick.   
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in 40 days from all; and therefore one must untie and administer baths and medicines of ointment to bring the place right.  
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and impeded, it remains to untie for 1 day or II months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of II bones, which are called the two «fosciles», because one is small, and that follows the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is below, towards the little hip; perhaps breaks the large foscile alone, or the small, and perhaps both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and made equal. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great cavity, then it is necessary to pull with more force; and extend it on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed on him-self, and the cushion in front of him higher, that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers of the arm to the part below his hand, or at the joint, and one other minister to the other above.  
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirror even, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each one in its place, and if any is detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, do as we have said before on the bone. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it comes with a bruise to the wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then glue a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, that it not be neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth above subtly, until the abscesses are appeased.  
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the osteologist removes the cerote, and puts on the plaster of the powder of the mill with an abundance of egg, then places the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be placed more forward, and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have VI splints or arms in more positions: either the fracture is in one of the bones, or in II; and restrain more above the fracture than elsewhere, and all days less in moving away, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the splint be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is strained be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until the itching is appeased; and let the limb not be allowed to rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so the address. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the nurse can't come to the limb because it is too swollen, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like this for some days until the swelling subsides, and then constrain it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not unbind him until XX days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when it is twisted, then he places his hands on his neck, and let his shoulders be even, and guard against movement and trembling, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and the complexions of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as well the palms many times have a few fractures, and there comes nothing but swelling many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or bent, it befits that the patient sit cross-legged, and stand straight in front of him also; then put his hand on the board stretched out, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them even in the middle, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the end of the plant near the belly, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to tighten it on their broken plant; and then strain with a long cloth, and let the splint be of hard wood as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as is fitting. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, then you must place a splint on top and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and close the ligature between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the two of us, that is the arm, set it even, as it should; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see that you put a small straight splinter to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other two, as in the index or one of the others, set it even, and bind it with the healthy joint that follows; or you tie them all in I holding, which is best, or you put on a splint, like the pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the disposition of the hot, dry abscess, and correct what comes to it, as I have said.  
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is this: one piece above the fracture, and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister his limb equally; and this is when the fracture is in the bone. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one ligament should be pulled towards the groin and the other ligaments below the fracture.  
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then be the bandage near the knee, and be the extension down; then put the pliers the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the tie, if an abscess does not come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, let it subside then return to your work and your care; the ligature is done in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you envelop the fracture with a stiff bandage doubled in II or III, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put I long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and make the head of the thread go up; then turn back on the leg and on the hip the bandage, then place above the fracture splints, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the space between the leg and the hip with cloth soft to put equal pressure, then begin to tie firmly III turns or IIII on the fracture; and as you go higher up the fracture, and less the restraint; then join the II heads of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and tie III splints that are above, then return down to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and the restraint, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as it is, then let there come neither abscess nor swelling nor other appearance.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so let it be untied and direct that which comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, so it is fitting to saw them, if one can; and if one cannot, so it is fitting to cut the place, and drain pus; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken like this, as in the shoulder and arm; however, during the restoration thus made, it does not hurt the patient at all. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the  hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the varieties of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer but a fracture, or opening, and it happens to all wounds, without wound, and everyone feels this well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: one puts it equal each which is rounded to its places, as long as it is assembled moved one can; then put the splint, and in it puts a round plate, if you have need of it, and restrain it as it befits, then reward all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar things; so put on each accident what it befits it, as long as it is sound. 
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, because one is called by right “mustelz”, and the other is called “foscile”; and there happen all kinds of fractures as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the works are all equal. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn it back. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well; and it turns below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer an extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are more pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to its virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take II bandages of woven strips that support the leg on one side and the other, and be of the length of the leg from the knee down; then wrap in them the two bandages above and below, and tie them in the middle, also, and at this joint, the leg will not be able to decline to the right or to the left, and so it is well; and none administer I bands along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and place it on the leg to ward off movement, and properly do this in the fracture or where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or another accident; so cure until it is healed. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones of the foot  
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the bones of the foot there is sometimes a fracture and at the two toes, and there have been very few in more dispositions. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there happen to be broken bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlap each other, put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he wanted to walk, then put now your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it so that they return into their places; then put the splint and dressings on, and put under the belly of the foot a small board at the two hips full, then restrain the foot firmly, then when you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things of which you have need.  
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when III days or IIII will have passed, untie the linen, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, then restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be a finger width wider, then put under the foot that table that I have said, and strain it evenly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and strain the table under the foot; and let it be standing on the top of the table, outside of the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.  
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to the other breaks, since we have said them; and secure each accident as it befits.  
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger 
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, so make her sit enlarged, then incline it to the part of the back, and be held by behind; then fill the basin of the woman's nature with cotton, and put in as large as the I sto; then take out the woman, and lift her back up and down, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with the sto; and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and so do VII days or around: so will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of lambs, and tie to the opening a chain, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the chain form, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and are not these fractures hidden from him who puts his study and his use to it, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies to more dispositions the right way of restoration: then therefore. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	On the branch, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the branch; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will be healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that they be healed now, so that the dressings that we have said testify to it.  
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing, then keep the vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come there, let the restoration wait until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then you must put it back together lightly with your hands, with small extension.  
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not ready for you to put equal in your hands, then resort to this instrument which is of iron, which has VII or VIII degrees of length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary for the mire that he grasps III or IV, according to what he needs in each cure of a sprain; and let it be round and one finger thick, so that it does not bend under compression upon the member at your work, and let it be thicker at the front and thicker from the middle forward, thus: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palainche", for which the shoulder should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it returns, and be equal to each other.  
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it behoves that you cut the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have purchase. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incisor or saw, to your power; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.  
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is so that it is in its place, then moisten the drape with black spiced wine, and properly if it has been placed; and do not put on the wound any cerate nor anything else where there is oil, lest it bring forth rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times have foolish people done this, and have brought upon the patient either death or corruption at any time; and let the constriction be softer and more sparing than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it does not behoove to put on dressings; but envelop around, instead of dressings, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound is starting to bulge, then remove what you have put on top of all wine, and put ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment tetra-formation and similar.  
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, the morning and evening, as long as it is healed and sound.  
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a manner that the bow be corrected down gently.  
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days it does not heal and cannot return to its place, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must cover the wound with a bandage, and remove all these dislocated pieces that cause pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other manner of corruption, then you must treat it according to what he says in his chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, do not set it, because many times death comes from it, but let it be until it decays; perhaps it will heal itself after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.  
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of boils which come from the swelling 
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and a sad thing is to see the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot do the limb its natural works. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed then if it is fresh: if he administers medicines astringent, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, just as you take any of these things, or all together, and you prepare them with astringent wine, or with white of egg, or with oil; and put it on the wound in compresses, and restrain it well, and do not release it in hands during days; and then loosen it, and begin another one, until the swelling is removed; or you restrain it on a piece of well-made wood; for the properties of wood are that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling is already converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above, and make the superfluity apparent; or you reapply it to any razor, until it is removed, and care until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and afterwards the limb remains weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: because one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and was not tied as it should; or because there were too many bindings, and it could not come to nourishment in the limb; or for a multitude of dressings; or for too great movements, not at the right time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, as long as the blood is multiplied in him; and administer bath, and give him joy and license; then put wool on the member, so that the wool attracts to the great swelling, and the rose often of cold water, until the swelling corrects to the member; and returns to its natural figure. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of member wrong after the health 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, however it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes great evils, and by chance death; however, if the nodules and the torments are fresh, then it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of wormwood, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and you take the wool of wormwood, and you confit it with fat of lard or oil of sesame, and make a plaster above; or you take figs grease, and grind them with chaff of wheat, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes is dislocation removed by continuously rubbing and lengthwise with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be exercised movement to the limb every hour.  
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is hardened and tough, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be cut up to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly; and put care and study into the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from any joint out of its place, because of which it cannot move, and the limb is poorly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.  
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it is necessary now to bring it back without resorting to splints.  
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limbs swell, and by chance if one tries to put it back in place; for this reason one should not move it when it is swollen: many times it brings pain and other pains; however, when this happens, first bleed the patient, then let him, until the abscesses are all calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as one would cure wounds. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated and the dislocations of both sides are according to two manners: either they are a little removed from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang toward the lower part, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with the word. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many more disarrangements. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it carefully, and do not hesitate; and in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and puts his fingers deep into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand should be outside, to put equal; and command the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the broken bone is placed even, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the bringing back is painful, even if it are the two mandibles together, apply hot water and oil, until they are gently reset; do not hesitate to bring it back as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is well closed with softened cloth, place on top cloths moistened in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with soft bindings; and let the sick person sleep on their back, and their shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor exerts himself to chew, but eats light food, as long as the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then suck what he wants lightly, and do not strain yourself to open your mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well healed and clean.  
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not brought back to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats come, and perhaps a solution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is perdition; and many times die those who have it, in IX days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork  
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The harness cannot dislocate from within the side and hip, and it is dislocated no times outward, and it is well felt when it is. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies flat on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place firmly with his palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it; and the head which is toward the side cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it dislocates at any time, put it back in its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and the bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus, same way is brought back the head of the shoulder, when it is out of place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one is when it is dislocated to the part of the seat towards the hip; and the second is to the part of the breast; and by chance dislocated to the upper part, which happens little; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated downwards towards the hip, especially in those who have little flesh, because on these it moves easily; on those who have enough flesh, it moves with difficulty, and returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder of a hot abscess, and believes that it is dislocated because of this. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must feel it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it is moved down toward the seat, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and under the seat toward touching the head of the shoulder, as if they were one bone; and the sick person cannot bring back his hand to its place, nor move any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly in touching; and this manner of dislocation is not otherwise than to be brought back, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient upwards, then put their hands under the seat, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place; and the ministers lift the hand and extend it upwards, then put it down; so it will come gradually.  
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and they administer a softening and soothing remedy, such as decoction of altea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be administered; then lie down the patient on his back, and put under the buttock a cushion of equal wool, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the patient on the cushion, and raise the head of the shoulder carefully, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that he does not move down; the shoulder returns now, and if you see it, reset it according to this manner: and it is that you make the man present who is greater than the patient; and let him be straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the buttock of the patient, and raise the buttock up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can carry with him anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another manner: and one takes a long stick into the earth, whose head is as long as the pistol, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is put under the patient, but that he has blankets above, and the patient lies on the long of the shaft; then it is extended his hand on the other side to form, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of II arms of great and IIII duodecims of wide, which has the head rounded to enter in profile under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then on the head of the staff drape cloths so that the staff doesn't rub against the patient, then place it under the seat of the patient; and extend his arm upon the staff long, and tie the assistant to the staff, and the arm to the hand's chief, then put the arm upon the step of a ladder wide, and let the hands be stretched down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint returns now. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that you put under the collar of a sphere of wool equal, then put the plaster parilliet of powder from the mill, with incense and auburn of an egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the collar evenly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.  
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he apply poultices, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal faster; and then apply them again after 5 days or 7, and move it; and if it is hard and not softened, it is healed.  
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another cause, then it is necessary that you administer cautery to three holes, as it is shown in the chapter on cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the hip, and the breasts, or back, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and there is administered in another place; and care until it be healed.  
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, then the patient uses many baths until that pain is relieved, and returns to its first nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the arm 
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated in points, and in points it returns; and if it is dislocated from all parts, and even before and behind, and the dislocation is not replaced, because it is seen well and felt well; and dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.  
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.  
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as abscesses come, because if abscesses came, it would be grievous to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back entirely in all, especially when it is at the rear; so it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and its arms be spread, and the hands touch each other according to the knife around, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulder together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is to the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and firm at the root of the palm its side which is dislocated.  
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension; and that two ministers stretch the arm, and they hold it tight so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in each direction, then when you have enveloped a double cloth long and wide; and when the hand joins the joint, he puts on oil of any kind to soften the joint, then thrust the joint together, until it comes back; and when it is in place, put on a dry plaster with yolk of an egg, and hold it firmly, and put the arm against the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie the linen, and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not tight, then re-begin the bandaging and linen, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is soothed; or you put on the joint a fleece of fat wool, then let it rest for a day and a night, then remove it, and let it go into the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the fleece back, and then go into the bath; and thus do II times or III, until it is healed; and if you see that, put on fleece of moist heated heather with butter, and strain it on; if it will return to its disposition.   
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the place does not swell, or that a hot abscess comes.  
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the putting back is that you put the injured hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he puts it equal, as if it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns; altogether, you should look if it is well in place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a table at extension and putting back. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts their back of their hand on the table, and the one caring for them puts their hand on that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good. If not, apply soothing ointments to the abscess, and leave it so as not to begin again.  
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the joint remains twisted; and harms nothing to the patient except that as long as his hand is numb, and cannot stretch anything at all: therefore know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; so there is no other means except to constrain with fire cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is not worth anything else. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then restrain it and let it be for 5 days, then untie it and leave as is.  
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then the hot water cloth, and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	At no time are the joints of the hand dislocated on each side, at no time on the back of the palm or on the belly; therefore are the joint, and thrust the dislocation to its pouches until it returns, then support the head of the joint, and the bend toward the part where it is disjoined; and leave it II days, and then put it even that day; and do not tie it, as we have said, and untie it each day, and make it move, and tie it again; and do this often, until it is straight, and just as well do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and just as well do, when it is dislocated on another part.   
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine  
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are more dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the articulations jump and move without will, and it cannot be held, and many times they are softened any limb, or the two thighs or the two arms or one.  And many times the knee moves to four parts; that which moves to the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure for this is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing of all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said many ways of cures with great words, which do not have at all much profit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast in front, there is nothing nor remedy; and also that which comes straight on II sides, and it cannot be cured except for that one properly which comes on the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is extended upon his face in I equal place, and has restraint under him, so that he does not move; then put the stick at the head in earth forming, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen between the shoulders of the sick person, and the other at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers take hold of the liens, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the II sticks; and let them be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine forming, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three arm lengths long, and place it under the arm, and the patient should be on their side, and put the head of the board under the arm, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and place his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, then do it with a turn that turns by hand.  
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you put II splints to the head of the sick man of an arm of great, and toward the feet II other, and have between each splint, up and down, a palm of space long; and have in each splint I hole, where the turn turns, and let the splints be firmly in earth, so that it does not move; and between each II splints have I turning splint, for which the linen turns, and have in II turning II small splints of a palm of long, to turn the turn; and then tie the linen that is among the splints to the turn toward the head, and the other linen toward the feet to the other turn, and each of the ministers turns his turn to the whole linen, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
