And when it is equal, put a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the tampons, and then the bandage of a tablet of III does long, which covers the place of the vertebrae and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a linen, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if any thing comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and relaxing medicines, with the bandage that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes it appears in the back vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocations; and it is the bone which opens, therefore one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come out as dislocations, and not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and less dislocated front and back.  
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the sick knee than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double their knee at all; and is the lews that are below swollen with hot abscesses because the head of the hip comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to the fever, so is this accident contrary to those before. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who has it in front are that his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nonetheless, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and he retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in the rear, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the hip is at the place under the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The return of this appearance of dislocation is that you should notice if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, if there is no cure; and it is not necessary that he have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of IV manners of dislocation, so haste that you return the joint, and the extension within and without, and the movement to right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other cure.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you appear the minister strong, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or at the ligament which should be tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upwards in such a manner that he puts his hands under his shoulders, then tightens a linen band above the hip; and one other holds the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to IV likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not so, it is necessary to put care to its appearance. When the dislocation is at the back, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the hip, and the part which is below the groin, then pull the linen up towards the groin, and towards the buttock; then take other ministers his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outwards in the form: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen band above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two more spans than the other; then let it be hung by the head from a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let another minister be hanging with the patient, who embraces the hip firmly, for the joint now returns readily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the back, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gilbosite, and restrain the linen on the bad leg properly, and on the hip too; then put two splints, one at the head and one at the feet, then put a splint between the thighs of the patient in the form; and have a plant of moist cloths around it, so that it does not become cold the bad limb, then extend each minister towards him, and the hand puts each part with his hand on the dislocation.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.  
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, place on a [table], and press it as we have said in the chapter on dislocations, and lay the patient on their healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the mirrors pain of being on the sore limb, then press with the other hand, and the extension down towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, it is not necessary to stretch the patient down or raise him up on the ground, but he must be as if the thigh were dislocated outside, as we have said about childbirth on the two hips; and be upon his face, and the bandage stretched as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint with the table; and it will be at point when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal; therefore adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then untie it, and put the splint on top; and if you see that they are equal, strap them as before, and leave it for three days; then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as much as he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and with other assistants extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he rests his leg at his hip lightly; and apply a plaster on it, and make the leg rest at the hip, and tie them together firmly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not allow the patient to walk, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel 
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes sprained, and sometimes dislocated completely, inside and outside. 
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it feels tender to the part where it is dislocated; the reinstatement is light, and one must extend it gently with his hands when it is only bruised. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, then you must make the patient sit straight, and hold him steady by one leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then up in the front, and push the foot well upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, because it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a stick firmly into the ground between his hips, and tie cloths around, so that the patient does not move; then hold the patient's hip with one minister, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the knee, so that they tie it on the neck of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the stick should be in place between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when being extended; then put the ministers equally at the dislocation with their hands, and other ministers hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is pointed, put the plaster and dressings on top, and strain them firmly, and tie his leg to his leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, that the ties be not too tight; then leave him for II days or III, and if the ties soften, tighten them again; then untie on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for IIII days; and if he goes before that term, it is not certain that he does not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come there, it is necessary that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed. 
des dois	of the two  
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to stretch them well without effort, and it is a light thing. 
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the knots of the back or of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his level or on a table perfectly straight, and put your foot upon what opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing open, then put under the sole of the foot a board at the shoulder, then strain firmly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and let him rest, as long as he is sound. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and tardy, nor bold; and use at the beginning of soothing things abscess hot, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place, so that the abscesses chaut may come; and when the limb is in its place, administer soothing things hot abscess, and cure the wound as it is proper, with drying ointments; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into fear's path, according to what I have said, for this will cause you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arms and body.
